Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
10 min
ضوابط المصلحة المرسلة وموقف الحنفية
Regulation of maslahah mursalah and Hanafi stance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the controls of maslahah mursalah to identify when a benefit qualifies as a valid source for a fatwa, and to contrast the Hanafi and Maliki approaches in a ruling derivation.

Core Idea
Maslahah mursalah must support a maqsad (daruri/haji/tahsini) and have no explicit text – otherwise, it is chaos.

In this passage, Mustafa al-Zarqa explains why uncontrolled maslahah leads to legal anarchy and how the early jurists, especially Malikis, set rigorous controls. He then clarifies the Hanafi position: they do not formally adopt maslahah mursalah but allow it indirectly through istihsan. This lesson unpacks the definition, the three maqasid categories, and the practical difference between the schools.

Guided Path
1
Define maslahah mursalah
Identify the two essential conditions: no explicit text (command or prohibition) dealing with the case by its specific wording or type, and that the benefit supports one of the three maqasid categories (daruriyyat, hajiyyat, tahsiniyyat).
Maslahah mursalah is 'unrestricted' because no text recognizes or cancels it.
2
Apply the control of non-contradiction with nass
If a text exists, scholars do not override it absolutely (contra al-Tufi); instead they have a nuanced, case-by-case approach.
This prevents maslahah from being used to disregard clear rulings.
3
Differentiate between ibadat and mu'amalat
Ibadat are ta'abbudi – no investigation into causes; maslahah reasoning applies only to worldly matters (customs, transactions).
This is a key Maliki distinction, accepted by all.
4
Contrast Hanafi and Maliki positions
Malikis openly adopt maslahah mursalah as a source. Hanafis reject it as independent, but their principle of istihsan opens a narrow door for it in practice.
Al-Qarafi notes that even deniers of maslahah mursalah often use it in detailed rulings.

الفصل (٥) المصادر التبعية : الاستصلاح
الشريعة الإسلامية خصبة مثرية منتجة مُشْبِعَةً لحاجات الناس في كل عصر وفي کل مکان (۱) (ر: كتاب «مالك» لأبي زهرة قسم ۲ ف/ ۱۸۷ و ۱۸۸).
٥ / ١٩ - ملاحظة :
يقول الأستاذ الجليل الشيخ محمد أبو زهرة في كتابه «ابن حنبل» بأن الحنفية كالشافعية لا يعتمدون المصالح المرسلة وليس لها في الاستدلال عندهم اعتبار، وإن كان الاستحسان عند الحنفية يفتح باباً قليلاً لها. كتاب ابن حنبل ص/ ۳۰۳).
وقد سبقه إلى هذا الآمدي في كتابه «أصول الأحكام».
(۱) يقول القرافي المالكي في كتابه تنقيح الفصول ص/ ٢٠٠/ : المصلحة المرسلة غيرنا يصرح بإنكارها، ولكنهم عند التفريع تجدهم يعللون بمطلق المصلحة، لا يطالبون أنفسهم عند الفروق والجوامع بابداء الشاهد لها بالاعتبار، بل يعتمدون على مجرد المناسبة - أي كون الشيء أنسب وأوفق ، هذا هو المصلحة المرسلة» ر كتاب «مالك» للأستاذ أبي زهرة القسم الثاني، ف/ ١٧٤ و ٢٠٩). وقد أوضح الإمام الشاطبي في كتابيه الموافقات» و «الاعتصام» وكذا غيره من الفقهاء الأصوليين النظار أن أحكام الشريعة قسمان :
الأول : ما يتعلق بشؤون الأخرة، وهو العبادات . والثاني: ما يتعلق بتنظيم شؤون الدنيا، وهو ما سوى العبادات من الأمور العادية والتعاملية ونحوها.
فالقسم الأول، أي العبادات لا يسوغ البحث فيه عن العلل والمصالح لربطه بها، وإنما الأمر فيه مبني على الاتباع التعبدي. - وأما القسم الثاني، وهو الذي يتكون منه تشريع النظم التعاملية، فإنه معلل بمصالح العباد، ومرتبط بالمعاني المصلحية في هذه الحياة كما تفيده نصوص الشريعة نفسها. وقد توسع الإمام مالك رضي الله عنه في النظر إلى تلك العلل والمعاني المصلحية في هذا القسم، حتى قال فيه بقاعدة المصالح المرسلة وبالاستحسان، وثبت عنه أنه قال: الاستحسان تسعة أعشار العالم) (ر: الموافقات ۳۰۷/۲).
وكتاب الموافقات هذا للإمام الشاطبي إبراهيم أبي إسحاق الغرناطي المتوفى سنة ٧٩٠ للهجرة هو أجل كتاب عرفناه في أصول الفقه ومقاصد الشريعة، أتى فيه مؤلفه الموفق رحمه الله بعجائب التفكير السديد والبصر الفقهي والأسلوب المبتكر، وهو
أربعة أجزاء .
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence
[From] nations this view absolutely in their legislation and permit it for men of rights and judiciary in their ijtihad, chaos would prevail in acting upon Shari'a and law: whoever perceives a benefit in the law acts by it, and whoever imagines harm in it abandons it, and in that is the utmost disorder and confusion (1).
Maslahah
Therefore, we found the imams and jurists of Islamic Shari'a unanimous in rejecting this extremism; and we saw that those who adopted the principle of istislah established, in the way of distinguishing [maslahah] from mafsadah and defining their limits, controls sufficient for this distinction and definition, derived from the general objectives of Shari'a which today are called the purpose of the Lawgiver, in order to prevent chaos in understanding and assessment, because maslahah and mafsadah must be defined according to the view of Shari'a and its consideration, not according to subjective or individual view, as previously explained in section 3/5-4.
(And we also saw that among the foremost of those controls established to prevent confusion through the path of istislah is that the maslahah on which the ruling is based must be a maslahah mursalah, i.e., there is no text in Shari'a commanding or prohibiting it, dealing with it specifically or by its type, and that it should support one of the three categories of rulings that organize social life: necessities (daruriyyat), needs (hajiyyat), and improvements (tahsiniyyat).
If a legal text conflicts with the maslahah, then the scholars do not give priority to the maslahah over the text absolutely as (al-Tufi) wanted; rather they have a detailed stance towards it which we will see soon (see section 20/5-25).
This is the position of istihsan and istislah among these four ijtihad schools (2). No doubt that adopting the methodology followed by Hanafi, Maliki, and Hanbali jurists makes
Islamic Shari'a fertile, enriching, productive, and satisfying the needs of people in every time and every place (1) (see: Kitab 'Malik' by Abu Zahra, section 2, pp. 187-188).
5/19 - Note:
The illustrious teacher Shaykh Muhammad Abu Zahra says in his book 'Ibn Hanbal' that the Hanafis like the Shafi'is do not rely on masalih mursalah and they have no consideration in inference, although istihsan among the Hanafis opens a small door for it. Kitab Ibn Hanbal p. 303.
Al-Amidi preceded him in this in his book 'Usul al-Ahkam'.
(1) Al-Qarafi al-Maliki says in his book Tangih al-Fusul p. 200: 'The maslahah mursalah - others explicitly deny it, but when it comes to branching you find them citing absolute maslahah, not requiring themselves to produce evidence for its consideration in distinctions and unifications, rather they rely on mere suitability - i.e., that a thing is more suitable and appropriate; this is the maslahah mursalah. See Kitab 'Malik' by Abu Zahra, section 2, pp. 174 and 209. Al-Imam al-Shatibi clarified in his two books al-Muwafaqat and al-I'tisam, as did other foundational jurists, that the rulings of Shari'a are of two types:
First: What pertains to matters of the Hereafter, which are acts of worship (ibadat). Second: What pertains to organizing worldly affairs, which are other than acts of worship, such as customary matters, transactions, and the like.
The first type, i.e., ibadat, does not permit investigation into their causes and masalih because of their connection to them; rather the matter is based on devotional following. As for the second type, which constitutes the legislation of transactional systems, it is caused by the masalih of the servants and linked to the maslahah meanings in this life as the texts of Shari'a themselves indicate. Imam Malik, may Allah be pleased with him, expanded in considering those causes and maslahah meanings in this type, to the extent that he adopted the principle of masalih mursalah and istihsan, and it is confirmed that he said: 'Istihsan is nine-tenths of knowledge' (see: al-Muwafaqat 2/307).
This book al-Muwafaqat by Imam al-Shatibi Ibrahim Abu Ishaq al-Gharnati, who died in 790 AH, is the greatest book we have known in usul al-fiqh and maqasid al-shari'a, in which its successful author, may Allah have mercy on him, brought wonders of sound thinking, juristic insight, and innovative style, and it is four volumes.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage discusses the subsidiary source of al-maslahah al-mursalah (unrestricted public interest) and its regulation in Islamic jurisprudence. The author, Mustafa al-Zarqa, explains the historical rejection of unrestricted maslahah by some, and the controls placed by those who accept it. He then notes the division of Shari'ah rulings into ibadat and mu'amalat, and the Maliki reliance on maslahah mursalah in the latter. A quote from Qarafi shows that even those who formally reject it often use it in practice. The passage also clarifies the Hanafi position: they do not formally adopt maslahah mursalah but accept it indirectly through istihsan.

Key Terms
المصلحة المرسلة (al-maslahah al-mursalah): مصلحة لم يرد في الشرع نص خاص باعتبارها أو إلغائها بعينها أو بنوعها، وتكون منضبطة بمقاصد الشرع العامة
الاستصلاح (al-istislah): العمل بالمصلحة المرسلة عند عدم وجود نص معارض
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): تعديل حكم القياس أو ترك القياس الجلي إلى قياس خفي أو نص أو عرف لمصلحة ترجح ذلك
الضروريات (al-daruriyyat): ما لا بد منه لقيام مصالح الدين والدنيا، كحفظ الدين والنفس والعقل والنسل والمال
الحاجيات (al-hajiyyat): ما يحتاج إليه الناس للتوسعة ورفع الحرج
التحسينيات (al-tahsiniyyat): ما يكون من مكارم الأخلاق ومحاسن العادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
ما موقف الحنفية من المصلحة المرسلة وفقًا للنص؟
A) يعتمدونها كمصدر أساسي مثل المالكية
B) لا يعتمدونها مطلقًا ولا حتى عبر الاستحسان
C) لا يعتمدونها كأصل مستقل، لكن الاستحسان يفتح بابًا قليلًا لها
D) يعتمدونها في العبادات فقط

Key Takeaway
Maslahah mursalah is a controlled subsidiary source; Hanafis reject it as independent but allow it indirectly through istihsan, while Malikis accept it openly in mu'amalat.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Acceptance of Masalih Mursala: A Terminological Difference
Refuting the claim that Hanafis reject Masalih Mursala

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Masalih Mursala, explain how it is incorporated through Istihsan, and evaluate the claim that Hanafis reject this source.

Core Idea
Hanafis accept Masalih Mursala through Istihsan; the dispute with Malikis is only terminological.

A common misconception holds that Hanafis, like Shafi'is, reject Masalih Mursala (unrestricted public interest) as a source of law. In this passage, al-Zarqa challenges that view, arguing that Hanafi jurisprudence actually embraces Masalih Mursala through its established principle of Istihsan. The difference with the Maliki school, he contends, is purely terminological: both schools achieve the same practical results, but they use different names for the underlying method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
The author notes that some scholars (e.g., Abu Zahra, al-Amidi) assert that Hanafis do not give weight to Masalih Mursala. Identify exactly what they claim and why.
This claim is based on observation that Hanafi usul books do not use the term 'Masalih Mursala'.
2
Examine the Hanafi theory of Istihsan
Recall that Istihsan means departing from a general analogical rule (qiyas) for a stronger consideration, often a maslaha. Hanafis have a well-developed theory of Istihsan.
Istihsan is a primary method in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the logical entailment
Al-Zarqa argues that if Hanafis accept departing from qiyas for a maslaha (Istihsan), then logically they must accept building rulings on maslaha when no qiyas opposes (Istislah).
The passage states: 'فلا يعقل أن من يقول بالاستحسان لا يقول بالاستصلاح' – It is not plausible that one who says Istihsan does not say Istislah.
4
Diagnose the terminological confusion
The terms 'Istihsan' and 'Masalih Mursala' became popular in different schools at different times. Hanafis used 'Istihsan' while Malikis used 'Masalih Mursala' for the same practical considerations.
The author emphasizes that the difference is in nomenclature, not substance.
5
Recognize the practical convergence
Both Hanafis and Malikis end up considering public interest in their legal rulings, but they express it differently. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is minimal.
A mufti from either school will arrive at similar results in many cases.

الفصل (٥) المصادر التبعية : الاستصلاح
الشريعة الإسلامية خصبة مثرية منتجة مُشْبِعَةً لحاجات الناس في كل عصر وفي کل مکان (۱) (ر: كتاب «مالك» لأبي زهرة قسم ۲ ف/ ۱۸۷ و ۱۸۸).
٥ / ١٩ - ملاحظة :
يقول الأستاذ الجليل الشيخ محمد أبو زهرة في كتابه «ابن حنبل» بأن الحنفية كالشافعية لا يعتمدون المصالح المرسلة وليس لها في الاستدلال عندهم اعتبار، وإن كان الاستحسان عند الحنفية يفتح باباً قليلاً لها. كتاب ابن حنبل ص/ ۳۰۳).
وقد سبقه إلى هذا الآمدي في كتابه «أصول الأحكام».
(۱) يقول القرافي المالكي في كتابه تنقيح الفصول ص/ ٢٠٠/ : المصلحة المرسلة غيرنا يصرح بإنكارها، ولكنهم عند التفريع تجدهم يعللون بمطلق المصلحة، لا يطالبون أنفسهم عند الفروق والجوامع بابداء الشاهد لها بالاعتبار، بل يعتمدون على مجرد المناسبة - أي كون الشيء أنسب وأوفق ، هذا هو المصلحة المرسلة» ر كتاب «مالك» للأستاذ أبي زهرة القسم الثاني، ف/ ١٧٤ و ٢٠٩). وقد أوضح الإمام الشاطبي في كتابيه الموافقات» و «الاعتصام» وكذا غيره من الفقهاء الأصوليين النظار أن أحكام الشريعة قسمان :
الأول : ما يتعلق بشؤون الأخرة، وهو العبادات . والثاني: ما يتعلق بتنظيم شؤون الدنيا، وهو ما سوى العبادات من الأمور العادية والتعاملية ونحوها.
فالقسم الأول، أي العبادات لا يسوغ البحث فيه عن العلل والمصالح لربطه بها، وإنما الأمر فيه مبني على الاتباع التعبدي. - وأما القسم الثاني، وهو الذي يتكون منه تشريع النظم التعاملية، فإنه معلل بمصالح العباد، ومرتبط بالمعاني المصلحية في هذه الحياة كما تفيده نصوص الشريعة نفسها. وقد توسع الإمام مالك رضي الله عنه في النظر إلى تلك العلل والمعاني المصلحية في هذا القسم، حتى قال فيه بقاعدة المصالح المرسلة وبالاستحسان، وثبت عنه أنه قال: الاستحسان تسعة أعشار العالم) (ر: الموافقات ۳۰۷/۲).
وكتاب الموافقات هذا للإمام الشاطبي إبراهيم أبي إسحاق الغرناطي المتوفى سنة ٧٩٠ للهجرة هو أجل كتاب عرفناه في أصول الفقه ومقاصد الشريعة، أتى فيه مؤلفه الموفق رحمه الله بعجائب التفكير السديد والبصر الفقهي والأسلوب المبتكر، وهو أربعة أجزاء .

ولكننا لا نرى هذا الحكم صواباً. فالحقيقة بالنسبة إلى الحنفية خلافه. وهم متفقون منبع المالكية كما بينا عندما صنفنا الاجتهادات بالنسبة إلى الاستحسان والاستصلاح.
فقد تقدَّم أنَّ الاجتهاد الحنفي قد أسس نظرية الاستحسان الذي هو كما رأينا خروج عن النظائر والقواعد القياسية العامة لوجهة أقوى أو لضرورة تقتضي مصلحة أو تدفع مفسدة.
فإذا كان الحنفية يقولون باعتبار المصلحة والخروج لأجلها استحساناً عن القواعد القياسية إذا عارضتها فإنهم يوجبون اعتبار المصلحة المرسلة وبناء الأحكام على مقتضاها بطريق الأولوية عندما لا تعارضها القواعد القياسية. وهذا هو معنى الاستصلاح كما تقدم في الفرق بين الاستحسان والاستصلاح . فلا يعقل أن من يقول بالاستحسان لا يقول بالاستصلاح، لأنَّ الاستحسان هو نهاية الشوط ؛ فمن بلغها فقد اجتاز ما دونها حتماً (ر ) المدخل إلى علم أصول الفقه للأستاذ الدكتور معروف الدواليبي ص ۲۸۷ - ۲۸۸ الطبعة الثانية) .
ولعل سبب هذا الاشتباه هو أنَّ اسم المصالح المرسلة قد ظهر وشاع في اصطلاح المالكية بعد أن ظهر وشاع اسم الاستحسان في اصطلاح الحنفية. فاختلاف الاسم كان مدعاة لهذا الاشتباه والظن.
فالفرق في نظرنا بين الحنفية والمالكية في هذا الموضوع إنما هو اختلاف في الاصطلاح، لا خلاف في الاستصلاح.
(1) والتمثيل الصحيح في نظرنا بين الحنفية والمالكية في هذا الموضوع هو أن النظر المصالح في بناء الأحكام الشرعية نظير طريق أحد رأسيه الاستحسان، والآخر الاستصلاح بالمعنى المشروح فيهما :
فالحنفية دخلوا من باب الاستحسان إلى الاستصلاح، والمالكية بالعكس، وكل منهما اشتهر بالباب الذي دخل منه .
Chapter (5): Subsidiary Sources: Istislah. The Islamic Sharia is fertile, enriching, productive, satisfying the needs of people in every age and every place (1) (See: Kitab 'Malik' by Abu Zahra, sect 2, pp. 187-188). 5/19 - Note: The venerable professor Sheikh Muhammad Abu Zahra says in his book 'Ibn Hanbal' that the Hanafis, like the Shafi'is, do not rely on Masalih Mursalah and they have no consideration for it in inference, although Istihsan among the Hanafis opens a small door for it. (Ibn Hanbal p. 303). Al-Amidi preceded him in this in his book 'Usul al-Ahkam'. (1) Al-Qarafi al-Maliki says in his book Tanqih al-Fusul p. 200: 'Others explicitly deny Maslaha Mursala, but when they branch out you find them giving reasons with absolute maslaha; they do not require themselves when distinguishing and combining to show evidence for it, but rely solely on appropriateness – i.e., something being more suitable and more fitting. This is Maslaha Mursala.' (See: Kitab 'Malik' by Abu Zahra, sect 2, pp. 174, 209). And Imam al-Shatibi explained in his books 'al-Muwafaqat' and 'al-I'tisam', as did other jurist-usul scholars, that the rulings of Sharia are of two types: The first: what pertains to matters of the Hereafter, which are acts of worship. The second: what pertains to organizing worldly affairs, which are matters other than worship, such as customs and transactions and the like. For the first type, i.e., acts of worship, it is not permissible to investigate the 'illah and interests linked to them; rather the matter is based on devotional following. As for the second type, from which the legislation of transactional systems is composed, it is reasoned by the interests of the servants and connected to beneficial meanings in this life, as the texts of Sharia themselves indicate. And Imam Malik – may Allah be pleased with him – expanded in looking at those 'illahs and beneficial meanings in this type, even to the point of adopting the principle of Masalih Mursala and Istihsan, and it is established from him that he said: 'Istihsan is nine-tenths of knowledge' (see: al-Muwafaqat 2/307). And this book al-Muwafaqat by Imam al-Shatibi Ibrahim Abi Ishaq al-Gharnati, who died in 790 AH, is the most esteemed book we know in Usul al-Fiqh and Maqasid al-Sharia; its successful author – may Allah have mercy on him – presented wonders of sound thinking, juristic insight, and innovative style. It is in four parts. But we do not consider this judgment correct. The truth regarding the Hanafis is the opposite. They are in agreement with the source of the Malikis, as we explained when we classified ijtihad concerning Istihsan and Istislah. For it has preceded that Hanafi ijtihad established the theory of Istihsan, which is, as we saw, departure from general analogical parallels and rules for a stronger viewpoint or for a necessity that requires an interest or repels corruption. So if the Hanafis say that consideration of interest and departing for its sake by way of Istihsan from analogical rules when they oppose it, then they necessarily require consideration of Maslaha Mursala and building rulings on its basis by way of precedence when analogical rules do not oppose it. This is the meaning of Istislah as previously explained in the difference between Istihsan and Istislah. So it is not plausible that one who says Istihsan does not say Istislah, because Istihsan is the ultimate stage; whoever reaches it has definitely passed what is below it (see: al-Madkhal ila 'Ilm Usul al-Fiqh by Prof. Dr. Ma'ruf al-Dawalibi, pp. 287-288, second edition). Perhaps the reason for this confusion is that the name 'Masalih Mursala' appeared and became widespread in Maliki terminology after the name 'Istihsan' appeared and became widespread in Hanafi terminology. The difference in names was a cause for this confusion and assumption. So the difference in our view between Hanafis and Malikis in this subject is merely a difference in terminology, not a difference regarding Istislah. (1) And the correct illustration in our view between Hanafis and Malikis in this subject is that consideration of interests in building legal rulings is like a road, one end of which is Istihsan and the other is Istislah with the meaning explained: the Hanafis entered from the door of Istihsan to Istislah, and the Malikis the opposite, and each became famous for the door from which he entered.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm addresses a common misconception about the Hanafi stance on Masalih Mursala (unrestricted public interest) as a subsidiary source of law. The author begins by noting that some scholars, like Muhammad Abu Zahra and al-Amidi, claim that Hanafis (like Shafi'is) do not rely on Masalih Mursala, allowing only a limited role through Istihsan. Al-Zarqa then refutes this, presenting the Hanafi position as essentially recognizing Masalih Mursala through the theory of Istihsan. He argues that Hanafi jurisprudence operates on the principle of departing from strict analogy (qiyas) when a stronger consideration or necessity demands it – that is Istihsan. But when no analogy opposes the interest, Hanafis apply the interest directly, which is precisely Istislah. Therefore, anyone who accepts Istihsan must logically accept Istislah, since Istihsan is the more advanced step. The author diagnoses the confusion as terminological: the Maliki school popularized the term 'Masalih Mursala', while the Hanafi school used 'Istihsan'. The difference is thus one of nomenclature, not substance. The passage concludes with a metaphor: consideration of interests is a road with two ends – Istihsan and Istislah – and the two schools approached from opposite ends, but they are on the same road.

Key Terms
الاستصلاح (al-istislah): The principle of basing legal rulings on consideration of public interest (maslaha) that is not explicitly recognized by a specific textual evidence (maslaha mursala).
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Departing from a general analogy (qiyas) for a stronger evidence or necessity that calls for a different ruling, often based on consideration of public interest.
المصلحة المرسلة (al-maslaha al-mursala): An unrestricted public interest that is not explicitly validated or invalidated by a specific scriptural text; it is a consideration for legal rulings in transactional and worldly matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Zarqa in this passage, what is the relationship between Istihsan and Istislah in Hanafi jurisprudence?
A) Istihsan and Istislah are completely separate and independent principles.
B) Istihsan is a subset of Istislah, since it is used only when analogy is present.
C) Istislah is automatically implied once Istihsan is accepted, because considering interest without conflicting analogy is the essence of Istislah.
D) Hanafis reject Istislah and only use Istihsan in specific cases.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis do accept Masalih Mursala; the dispute with the Malikis is merely terminological, both achieving the same practical result through different nomenclature.

Hanafi and Maliki Positions on Istihsan and Istislah
Clarifying the terminological difference between Hanafi and Maliki on maslaha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi view on maslaha mursala through istihsan and evaluate the claim that the difference with Malikis is only terminological.

Core Idea
The difference between Hanafis and Malikis on maslaha mursala is terminological, not substantive—both consider public interest, just through different doors.

This passage addresses a common misconception that Hanafis reject the concept of maslaha mursala (unrestricted public interest). Dr. Mustafa al-Zarqa argues that Hanafis incorporate public interest through their well-established principle of istihsan, which permits departure from analogical reasoning for a stronger cause. Understanding this terminological overlap is crucial for any mufti navigating between Hanafi and Maliki reasoning in contemporary fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Locate the opening sentence where the author rejects a previous ruling that Hanafis do not consider maslaha mursala. This sets the stage for his counter-argument.
The claim is that Hanafis ignore unrestricted public interest as a source.
2
Understand Hanafi istihsan
Review the author's description of istihsan as departure from qiyas for a stronger consideration or necessity. This is the foundation of their approach to public interest.
Istihsan is a recognized source in the Hanafi school, defined as preference for a weaker analogy over a stronger one due to a superior consideration.
3
Link istihsan to istislah
Follow the author's logic: if Hanafis use istihsan to favour benefit when qiyas conflicts, they naturally must accept istislah (unrestricted benefit) when no qiyas conflict exists. This is presented as a priority argument (bi tariq al-awlawiyya).
The author emphasizes that istihsan is the 'ultimate extent'—whoever reaches it has necessarily passed the lower stage of istislah.
4
Analyze the terminological difference
Note the author's explanation that the confusion arises because the term 'masalih mursala' became popular among Malikis after 'istihsan' became popular among Hanafis. The difference is therefore in naming, not substance.
This is the core thesis: terminological variation, not methodological opposition.
5
Synthesize the mufti's takeaway
Conclude that for fatwa purposes, both schools effectively consider public interest. The Hanafi mufti should recognize that istihsan encompasses maslaha mursala, and the Maliki approach is complementary, not contradictory.
This alignment is important for inter-madhhab understanding and when adopting positions from other schools.

الباب الثاني : مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
ولكننا لا نرى هذا الحكم صواباً. فالحقيقة بالنسبة إلى الحنفية خلافه. وهم متفقون منبع المالكية كما بينا عندما صنفنا الاجتهادات بالنسبة إلى الاستحسان والاستصلاح.
فقد تقدَّم أنَّ الاجتهاد الحنفي قد أسس نظرية الاستحسان الذي هو كما رأينا خروج عن النظائر والقواعد القياسية العامة لوجهة أقوى أو لضرورة تقتضي مصلحة أو تدفع مفسدة.
فإذا كان الحنفية يقولون باعتبار المصلحة والخروج لأجلها استحساناً عن القواعد القياسية إذا عارضتها فإنهم يوجبون اعتبار المصلحة المرسلة وبناء الأحكام على مقتضاها بطريق الأولوية عندما لا تعارضها القواعد القياسية. وهذا هو معنى الاستصلاح كما تقدم في الفرق بين الاستحسان والاستصلاح . فلا يعقل أن من يقول بالاستحسان لا يقول بالاستصلاح، لأنَّ الاستحسان هو نهاية الشوط؛ فمن بلغها فقد اجتاز ما دونها حتماً (ر المدخل إلى علم أصول الفقه للأستاذ الدكتور معروف الدواليبي ص ۲۸۷ - ۲۸۸ الطبعة الثانية). 
ولعل سبب هذا الاشتباه هو أنَّ اسم المصالح المرسلة قد ظهر وشاع في اصطلاح المالكية بعد أن ظهر وشاع اسم الاستحسان في اصطلاح الحنفية. فاختلاف الاسم كان مدعاة لهذا الاشتباه والظن.
فالفرق في نظرنا بين الحنفية والمالكية في هذا الموضوع إنما هو اختلاف في الاصطلاح، لا خلاف في الاستصلاح
(1) والتمثيل الصحيح في نظرنا بين الحنفية والمالكية في هذا الموضوع هو أن النظر إلى المصالح في بناء الأحكام الشرعية نظير طريق أحد رأسيه الاستحسان، والآخر الاستصلاح بالمعنى المشروح فيهما:
فالحنفية دخلوا من باب الاستحسان إلى الاستصلاح، والمالكية بالعكس، وكل منهما اشتهر بالباب الذي دخل منه.
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence. But we do not see this ruling as correct. The truth regarding the Hanafis is otherwise. They agree with the source of the Malikis as we explained when we categorized ijtihad in relation to istihsan and istislah. It has been earlier mentioned that Hanafi ijtihad established the theory of istihsan, which, as we have seen, is a departure from general analogical precedents and rules for a stronger consideration or for a necessity that demands a benefit or repels a harm. If the Hanafis consider benefit and depart for its sake as istihsan from the analogical rules when they conflict with it, then they obligate consideration of unrestricted benefit (maslaha mursala) and building rulings upon its requirement by priority when analogical rules do not conflict with it. This is the meaning of istislah as previously explained in the difference between istihsan and istislah. It is unreasonable that one who says istihsan does not say istislah, because istihsan is the ultimate extent; whoever reaches it has necessarily passed what is below it. (Ref: al-Madkhal ila 'Ilm Usul al-Fiqh by Prof. Dr. Ma'ruf al-Dawalibi, pp. 287-288, second edition). Perhaps the reason for this confusion is that the term masalih mursala appeared and became widespread in Maliki terminology after the term istihsan appeared and became widespread in Hanafi terminology. So the difference in name was a cause for this confusion and assumption. The difference in our view between Hanafis and Malikis on this subject is only a difference in terminology, not a difference in istislah. (1) The correct illustration in our view between Hanafis and Malikis on this subject is that considering benefits in building legal rulings is like a path with two ends: one is istihsan and the other is istislah with the meaning explained for them. The Hanafis entered through the door of istihsan to istislah, and the Malikis vice versa, and each school became famous for the door through which it entered.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage addresses the relationship between istihsan and istislah in the Hanafi and Maliki schools. The author begins by rejecting a claim that Hanafis do not consider maslaha mursala. He explains that Hanafi ijtihad established istihsan as a departure from qiyas for a stronger reason or necessity, which inherently gives weight to public interest. Since istihsan also considers maslaha when qiyas conflicts, it logically follows that Hanafis must also accept maslaha mursala (istislah) when no qiyas conflict exists, because istihsan is a higher stage. The author attributes the confusion to the chronological and terminological difference: the term 'masalih mursala' became popular among Malikis while 'istihsan' became popular among Hanafis. He concludes that the difference is purely terminological, not substantive. A final analogy describes the two schools as entering the same concept through different doors: Hanafis from istihsan to istislah, Malikis from istislah to istihsan.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A Hanafi principle of departing from analogical reasoning for a stronger consideration, such as public benefit or necessity.
الاستصلاح (al-istislah): The Maliki principle of considering unrestricted public interest (maslaha mursala) as a basis for legislation when no text or qiyas applies.
المصالح المرسلة (al-masalih al-mursala): Unrestricted benefits that are not explicitly recognized or rejected by the primary sources, used as a source of law in the Maliki school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A terminological difference only
C) A difference in the definition of qiyas
D) A difference in the authority of ijma'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts maslaha mursala through the principle of istihsan; the difference with the Maliki school is terminological, not substantive.

Conflict Between Maslaha Mursala and Sacred Texts
Explaining hierarchy when maslaha conflicts with specific or general texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a maslaha mursala is overridden by a specific text and apply the principle that texts take precedence.

Core Idea
A specific sacred text always overrides a conflicting maslaha mursala — benefit cannot trump revealed command.

In this lesson, we explore a critical rule in Hanafi usul: what happens when a public interest (maslaha mursala) conflicts with an existing textual evidence. The passage clarifies that the default assumption — no text present — is what allows maslaha to operate. But if a text exists, especially a specific one, the text prevails. This is demonstrated by the prophetic prohibition of proposing over a brother's proposal.

Guided Path
1
Define maslaha mursala
Recall the definition: maslaha mursala is a benefit that agrees with maqasid but has no specific text or analogical basis.
This definition sets the scope of its application.
2
Identify the scenario of conflict
Understand the question: what happens when a maslaha that seems beneficial runs into a clear sacred text?
The passage assumes the text is preventing (mani’).
3
Classify the type of text
Distinguish between specific (khass) and general ('amm) texts. Specific texts apply to limited cases; general texts cover many instances.
The example given is a specific text (hadith).
4
Apply the hierarchy
Decide: when a specific text exists, it must be followed. The ruling is attributed to the text, not to the maslaha.
This principle ensures primacy of revelation over human reasoning.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (٥) المصادر التبعية : الاستصلاح
٢٠/٥ - تعارض المصالح المرسلة مع نصوص الشريعة :

رأينا فيما سلف من تعريف المصلحة المرسلة أنها هي المصلحة التي تتفق والمقاصد العامة للشريعة دون أن يكون هناك نص شرعي عليها أو ما يماثلها بحيث يمكن أن تقاس عليه. فالمفروض إذن في الأمور والأحكام التي يبنيها الاجتهاد الفقهي على قاعدة المصالح أنه لا يوجد نص شرعي يأمر بها، أو يأمر بأمر تجمعها به علة مماثلة بحيث يمكن أن تقاس عليه؛ إذ لو كان مثل هذا النص موجوداً في الموضوع لكان الحكم المطلوب مضافاً إليه أو إلى القياس المبني عليه، لا إلى مجرد المصلحة التي أوجب الشرع الإسلامي رعايتها بوجه عام (ر: ف ١/٥). ولكن العكس ممكن التصور والوقوع، وهو أن يعترض سبيل المصلحة المتفقة مع مقاصد الشريعة نص شرعي مانع، فهل يعمل عندئذ بالنص دون المصلحة أو بالمصلحة دون النص؟ وما هو الموقف الفقهي في ذلك؟

إن النصوص الشرعية نوعان:
- نصوص خاصة ترد عن الشارع في أشياء محدودة، وحالات معينة مخصوصة فتأمر بها أو تنهى عنها بخصوصها.
- ونصوص عامة ذات شمول وإحاطة يدخل تحت حكمها أمور كثيرة.
(1) كنهي النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن خطبة الإنسان على خطبة أخيه، أو سومه على سوم أخيه. - أخرجه البخاري (٥١٤٤)، ومسلم: ۲ : ۱۰۲۹ (۳۸) - أي لا يجوز لأحد، إذا رأى غيره يخطب امرأة للزواج، أو يساوم بائعاً على شيء ليشتريه منه، أن يأتي هو فيزاحمه على الخطبة أو الشراء، بل عليه أن ينتظر، فإذا لم يتم الاتفاق بين الطرفين تقدم هو للطلب.
Chapter (5) Subsidiary Sources: Istislah. 20/5 - Conflict of Unrestricted Benefits (Masalih Mursala) with Sacred Texts:

We have seen in the preceding definition of al-maslaha al-mursala that it is the benefit which agrees with the general objectives of the Shari'ah without there being a sacred text about it or something similar to it that can be analogically compared to it. Therefore, it is assumed in matters and rulings that fiqh ijtihad builds on the basis of benefits that there is no sacred text commanding them, or commanding a matter that they share with it a similar ratio legis such that they can be analogized to it; for if such a text existed on the subject, the required ruling would be attributed to it or to the analogy built upon it, not to mere benefit that Islamic law obligates taking care of in general (ref: 1/5). But the opposite is conceivable and occurs, which is that a preventing sacred text stands in the way of the benefit that agrees with the objectives of the Shari'ah. So should we act according to the text without the benefit or according to the benefit without the text? And what is the juristic position on that?

Sacred texts are of two types:
- Specific texts that come from the Lawgiver regarding limited things and specific particular cases, commanding or prohibiting them specifically.
- And general texts that are comprehensive and encompassing, under whose ruling many matters fall.
(1) Such as the Prophet's (peace be upon him) prohibition of a person proposing marriage over the proposal of his brother, or selling over the sale of his brother. - Narrated by al-Bukhari (5144) and Muslim: 2:1029 (38) - i.e., it is not permissible for anyone, if he sees another proposing to a woman for marriage, or bargaining with a seller for something to buy, to come and compete with him in the proposal or purchase; rather, he must wait. If the agreement between the two parties is not concluded, then he may proceed with his request.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage discusses the application of maslaha mursala (unrestricted public interest) as a subsidiary source of Islamic law. It begins by reiterating the definition: maslaha mursala is a benefit that aligns with the general objectives of the Shari'ah but has no specific textual evidence (nass) or something analogous that allows qiyas. The passage then raises a fundamental question: what happens when such a benefit conflicts with an existing text? The author explains that texts are of two types: specific (khass) and general ('amm). The default assumption is that maslaha mursala operates only where no text exists. If a text exists, especially a specific one, it takes precedence over mere benefit. To illustrate, he cites the hadith prohibiting proposing over a brother's proposal or selling over his sale—this is a specific text that prevents a seemingly beneficial action (competition) because the text forbids it. Thus, the juristic position is clear: when a text (especially specific) conflicts with a maslaha, the text prevails.

Key Terms
المصلحة المرسلة (al-maslaha al-mursala): A benefit that aligns with Shari'ah objectives but has no specific textual evidence or analogical basis.
نص خاص (nass khass): A sacred text that addresses a specific situation or ruling, not a general principle.
نص عام (nass 'amm): A sacred text with general application covering many cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The maslaha takes precedence over the text
B) The specific text takes precedence
C) A new ijtihad is required to reconcile them
D) The general text takes precedence

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when a specific text exists, it must be followed even if a maslaha mursala suggests a different outcome.

Legal Philosophy and Theory

Understanding Maslaha Mursala and Its Limits
Defining maslaha mursala and classifying nusus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define maslaha mursala, identify its conditions for validity, and classify Shariah texts by specificity and certainty.

Core Idea
Maslaha mursala is valid only when no qati' text exists; a perceived maslaha opposing a qati' text is actually a mafsada.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of maslaha mursala as a subsidiary source of Islamic law. Mustafa al-Zarqa explains its definition and the conditions under which it can be invoked. We also learn how Shariah texts are categorized into specific vs. general and definitive vs. speculative, which determines whether a maslaha can override them.

Guided Path
1
Define maslaha mursala
State the definition: a maslaha that aligns with Shariah objectives but has no direct textual evidence or analogy.
Key: it is not explicitly recognized or rejected by a text.
2
Distinguish specific vs. general texts
Identify whether a nass is specific (khas) or general ('amm). General texts cover many similar cases.
Example: prohibition of gharar is a general text.
3
Distinguish qati' vs. zanni texts
A text can be definitive (qati') in its indication (dalala) and/or transmission (thubut). If both are qati', it cannot be overridden.
Most general texts are considered zanni by the majority except Hanafis.
4
Apply the condition for maslaha
Maslaha mursala is only considered when there is no qati' text opposing it. If a qati' text exists, the maslaha is illusory.
The example of 'iddah shows a qati' text that cannot be set aside by maslaha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (٥) المصادر التبعية : الاستصلاح

٢٠/٥ - تعارض المصالح المرسلة مع نصوص الشريعة :

رأينا فيما سلف من تعريف المصلحة المرسلة أنها هي التي تتفق والمقاصد العامة للشريعة دون أن يكون هناك نص شرعي عليها أو ما يماثلها بحيث يمكن أن تقاس عليه .

فالمفروض إذن في الأمور والأحكام التي يبنيها الاجتهاد الفقهي على قاعدة المصالح أنه لا يوجد نص شرعي يأمر بها، أو يأمر بأمر تجمعها به علة مماثلة بحيث يمكن أن تقاس عليه ؛ إذ لو كان مثل هذا النص موجوداً في الموضوع لكان الحكم المطلوب مضافاً إليه أو إلى القياس المبني عليه، لا إلى مجرد المصلحة التي أوجب الشرع الإسلامي رعايتها بوجه عام (ر: ف ١/٥).

ولكن العكس ممكن التصور، والوقوع وهو أن يعترض سبيل المصلحة المتفقة مع مقاصد الشريعة نص شرعي مانع، فهل يعمل عندئذ بالنص دون المصلحة أو بالمصلحة دون النص؟ ما هو الموقف الفقهي في ذلك؟

إن النصوص الشرعية نوعان :
- نصوص خاصة ترد عن الشارع في أشياء محدودة، وحالات معينة مخصوصة فتأمر بها أو تنهى عنها بخصوصها
- ونصوص عامة ذات شمول وإحاطة يدخل تحت حكمها أمور وحالات وأفراد كثيرة متجانسة (1)

ثم إنَّ النص الشرعي قد يكون قطعياً في دلالته على المعنى المراد، وفي ثبوت نقله عن الشارع ؛ وقد يكون غير قطعي في إحدى هاتين الجهتين: أي الدلالة، أو الثبوت (2)

٢١/٥ - أ - المصلحة تجاه النص القطعي :

فإذا كان النص قطعياً في دلالته وثبوته لا يتصور أن تعارضه مصلحة تقتضي خلافه، لأن معيار المصلحة هو النظر الشرعي.

فما نظنه مصلحة بنظرنا الخاص وهو معارض لنص قطعي هو عندئذ مفسدة في نظر الشارع من وجوه أخرى راجحة فلا شك في لزوم العمل بالنص دون هذه المصلحة الموهومة وهذا مُتَّفق عليه بين أئمة فقهاء الشريعة، إلا بعض شذوذات فردية من أناس كسليمان الطوفي .

مثال ذلك أنَّ القرآن قد أوجب على المرأة المتزوجة، عند انحلال الزواج بالطلاق أن تتربص (أي تنتظر دون زواج جديد مدة ثلاثة أدوار طمثية إن كانت تحيض، أو ثلاثة أشهر إن كانت لا تحيض). وعند التأيم،

(1) كنهي النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن خطبة الإنسان على خطبة أخيه، أو سومه على سوم أخيه . - أخرجه البخاري (٥١٤٤) ، ومسلم : ۲ : ۱۰۲۹ (۳۸) ـ أي لا يجوز لأحد، إذا رأى غيره يخطب امرأة للزواج، أو يساوم بائعاً على شيء ليشتريه منه، أن يأتي هو فيزاحمه على الخطبة أو الشراء، بل عليه أن ينتظر ، فإذا لم يتم الاتفاق بين الطرفين تقدم هو للطلب .

(1) كنهي النبي عليه السلام عن بيع الغَرَر (بفتحتين)، قال ابن الأثير في «جامع الأصول» ٥٢٧/١ : الغرر ما له ظاهر تؤثره وباطن تكرهه فظاهره يغرُ المشتري، وباطنه مجهول) انتهى. فبيع الأشياء الاحتمالية غير المحققة الوجود أو الحدود، منهي عنه لما فيه من مغامرة وتغرير يجعله أشبه بالقمار كبيع ضربة القانص أو الغائص، أي ما ستخرجه شبكة الصياد من سمك، أو غوصة الغواص من لؤلؤ . فهذا نص عام يدخل جميع أنواع الغرر وانظر ما سيأتي في معنى النص العام ف ٢/٧١). هذا القبيل، أي غير القطعي جميع النصوص العامة في القرآن أو في السنة النبوية في نظر معظم أئمة الفقه الإسلامي سوى الحنفية فإن النص العام هو في نظر الأئمة غير قطعي الدلالة بسبب عمومه وكذا نصوص الحديث النبوي الثابتة برواية الآحاد ولو بطرق صحيحة فإنها عندهم غير قطعية الثبوت بوجه عام، ولو كانت قطعية الدلالة على المعنى المراد . (2)
Chapter (5): Subsidiary Sources: Istislah

20/5 - Conflict of Mursal Interests with Shariah Texts:

We have previously seen in the definition of maslaha mursala that it is that which agrees with the general objectives of the Shariah without there being a Shariah text concerning it or anything similar to it such that it could be analogized to it.

So it is assumed, therefore, in matters and rulings that ijtihad in fiqh builds upon the principle of maslaha, that there is no Shariah text commanding them, or commanding something that shares a similar ratio legis (illa) with them such that they could be analogized to it; for if such a text existed on the subject, the desired ruling would be attributed to it or to the analogy based upon it, not to mere maslaha, which Islamic law has required to be observed in general (cf. §1/5).

But the opposite is conceivable and occurs, namely that a preventing Shariah text obstructs the path of a maslaha that agrees with the objectives of the Shariah. So in that case, does one act upon the text and ignore the maslaha, or upon the maslaha and ignore the text? What is the juristic position on that?

Indeed, Shariah texts are of two types:
- Specific texts that come from the Lawgiver concerning limited things and specific individual cases, commanding or prohibiting them specifically.
- And general texts that have comprehensiveness and encompassment; under their ruling enter many similar matters, cases, and individuals (1).

Furthermore, a Shariah text may be definitive (qat'i) in its indication (dalala) of the intended meaning and in the certainty of its transmission (thubut) from the Lawgiver; and it may be non-definitive in one of these two aspects: either indication or transmission (2).

21/5 - A. The Maslaha in the Face of a Qat'i Text:

If the text is definitive in its indication and transmission, it is inconceivable that a maslaha could oppose it necessitating something contrary, because the criterion of maslaha is the Shariah's consideration.

So what we deem to be a maslaha according to our own opinion while it contradicts a qat'i text is, in that case, a mafsada (source of harm) in the view of the Lawgiver from other preponderant aspects. There is no doubt about the necessity of acting upon the text and ignoring this illusory maslaha. This is agreed upon by the imams and jurists of the Shariah, except for some individual exceptions like Sulayman al-Tufi.

An example of that is that the Qur'an has obligated upon a married woman, upon dissolution of marriage by divorce, to observe an 'iddah (i.e., wait without new marriage) for a period of three menstrual cycles if she menstruates, or three months if she does not menstruate. And regarding the widow, ...

(1) Such as the Prophet's prohibition (peace be upon him) of a person proposing marriage over the proposal of his brother, or bargaining over the bargain of his brother. Reported by Bukhari (5144) and Muslim (2:1029, no. 38). That is, it is not permissible for anyone, if he sees another person proposing to a woman for marriage, or negotiating with a seller over something to buy from him, to come and crowd him in the proposal or purchase; rather, he must wait, and if the two parties do not reach an agreement, he may then come forward with his request.

(1) Such as the Prophet's prohibition (peace be upon him) of the sale of gharar (uncertainty). Ibn al-Athir said in Jam' al-Usul (1/527): "Gharar is that which has an appealing exterior and a disliked interior; its exterior deceives the buyer, and its interior is unknown." Therefore, selling probabilistic things whose existence or boundaries are not ascertained is prohibited because it involves risk and deception that makes it resemble gambling, such as selling the catch of a hunter or diver, i.e., whatever the fisherman's net brings out or the diver's dive brings up. This is a general text that includes all types of gharar. See also the coming discussion on the meaning of the general text in §2/71). This kind, i.e., non-definitive, includes all general texts in the Qur'an or in the Sunna according to most imams of Islamic fiqh except the Hanafis. For the general text is, in the view of the imams [of the majority], non-definitive in indication due to its generality; likewise, texts of prophetic hadith established through ahad (solitary) transmission, even if through authentic chains, are generally non-definitive in transmission in their view, even if they are definitive in indication of the intended meaning. (2)
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a legal-philosophical discussion on the nature of maslaha mursala (unrestricted public interest) as a subsidiary source of Islamic law. The author, Mustafa al-Zarqa, first recaps the definition: maslaha mursala is a consideration that aligns with the general objectives of Shari'ah but lacks a specific textual proof (nass) or a clear analogy (qiyas) to such a proof. The core issue arises when a recognized maslaha conflicts with an existing nass. The passage then categorizes nusus into specific and general, and further divides them by certainty: qat'i (definitive) and zanni (speculative). The key ruling is that if a nass is qat'i in both its indication and transmission, no maslaha can override it, because what appears to us as a benefit but contradicts a definitive text is actually a harm (mafsada) from the divine perspective. This principle is universally accepted among jurists, with only rare dissenters like Ibn Taymiyya's student al-Tufi. The example given is the fixed 'iddah (waiting period) for divorced women, which cannot be replaced by any perceived maslaha. The footnotes illustrate specific nusus (like the prohibition of proposing over a brother's proposal) and general nusus (like the prohibition of gharar sales). Importantly, the author notes a Hanafi difference: general texts (umum) are considered zanni in dalala by the majority, but the Hanafis regard them as qat'i until evidence of specification arises. This passage is foundational for understanding the limits of ijtihad based on maslaha and the supremacy of definitive texts.

Key Terms
المصلحة المرسلة (al-maslaha al-mursala): مصلحة لا يشهد لها نص شرعي بالاعتبار ولا بالإلغاء، ولكنها توافق مقاصد الشريعة العامة
النص القطعي (al-nass al-qat'i): النص الثابت بالدليل القطعي الذي لا يقبل التأويل في دلالته أو ثبوته
النص العام (al-nass al-'amm): النص الذي يستغرق أفراداً كثيرة متجانسة بحكم واحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for maslaha mursala to be considered?
A) It must be agreed upon by all scholars.
B) There must be no qat'i text opposing it.
C) It must be based on a hadith.
D) It must be supported by qiyas jali.

Key Takeaway
Maslaha mursala is only valid in the absence of a qat'i text; a qat'i text always prevails.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
10 min
The Rule of Conflict: Maslaha vs. Qat'i Texts
Rule on conflict between maslaha and qat'i texts, and Hanafi view on umum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a qat'i text cannot be overridden by maslaha, and evaluate the Hanafi position that general texts are qat'i in indication until specified.

Core Idea
A qat'i text cannot be opposed by any maslaha; what seems a benefit is actually a harm. Hanafis treat general texts as qat'i until takhsis.

This lesson builds on the previous one by focusing on the specific scenario where a maslaha conflicts with a definitive text. Mustafa al-Zarqa emphasizes that such maslaha is illusory (mawhumah). We also examine the Hanafi view on general texts ('umum) which they consider qat'i in dalala, unlike the majority. This has practical implications for ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
State the rule on qat'i texts
If a nass is qat'i in both dalala and thubut, no maslaha can override it. The maslaha is actually a mafsada from the Shariah perspective.
This is agreed upon by all mainstream scholars except al-Tufi.
2
Apply to the 'iddah example
The Qur'an prescribes 'iddah for divorced and widowed women. Any claimed maslaha to shorten or eliminate it is invalid because the text is qat'i.
This shows that even if the maslaha seems rational, the text prevails.
3
Examine the Hanafi view on general texts
The Hanafis consider general texts ('amm) as qat'i in dalala until evidence of specification (takhsis) is found. The majority consider them zanni due to the possibility of takhsis.
Thus, for Hanafis, a general text can override a maslaha just like a specific qat'i text.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: In Hanafi, a general text like 'do not sell gharar' is immediately binding and cannot be set aside by maslaha, whereas the majority might allow a maslaha if the general text is considered zanni.
This affects rulings on modern contracts with uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (٥) المصادر التبعية : الاستصلاح

٢٠/٥ - تعارض المصالح المرسلة مع نصوص الشريعة :

رأينا فيما سلف من تعريف المصلحة المرسلة أنها هي التي تتفق والمقاصد العامة للشريعة دون أن يكون هناك نص شرعي عليها أو ما يماثلها بحيث يمكن أن تقاس عليه .

فالمفروض إذن في الأمور والأحكام التي يبنيها الاجتهاد الفقهي على قاعدة المصالح أنه لا يوجد نص شرعي يأمر بها، أو يأمر بأمر تجمعها به علة مماثلة بحيث يمكن أن تقاس عليه ؛ إذ لو كان مثل هذا النص موجوداً في الموضوع لكان الحكم المطلوب مضافاً إليه أو إلى القياس المبني عليه، لا إلى مجرد المصلحة التي أوجب الشرع الإسلامي رعايتها بوجه عام (ر: ف ١/٥).

ولكن العكس ممكن التصور، والوقوع وهو أن يعترض سبيل المصلحة المتفقة مع مقاصد الشريعة نص شرعي مانع، فهل يعمل عندئذ بالنص دون المصلحة أو بالمصلحة دون النص؟ ما هو الموقف الفقهي في ذلك؟

إن النصوص الشرعية نوعان :
- نصوص خاصة ترد عن الشارع في أشياء محدودة، وحالات معينة مخصوصة فتأمر بها أو تنهى عنها بخصوصها
- ونصوص عامة ذات شمول وإحاطة يدخل تحت حكمها أمور وحالات وأفراد كثيرة متجانسة (1)

ثم إنَّ النص الشرعي قد يكون قطعياً في دلالته على المعنى المراد، وفي ثبوت نقله عن الشارع ؛ وقد يكون غير قطعي في إحدى هاتين الجهتين: أي الدلالة، أو الثبوت (2)

٢١/٥ - أ - المصلحة تجاه النص القطعي :

فإذا كان النص قطعياً في دلالته وثبوته لا يتصور أن تعارضه مصلحة تقتضي خلافه، لأن معيار المصلحة هو النظر الشرعي.

فما نظنه مصلحة بنظرنا الخاص وهو معارض لنص قطعي هو عندئذ مفسدة في نظر الشارع من وجوه أخرى راجحة فلا شك في لزوم العمل بالنص دون هذه المصلحة الموهومة وهذا مُتَّفق عليه بين أئمة فقهاء الشريعة، إلا بعض شذوذات فردية من أناس كسليمان الطوفي .

مثال ذلك أنَّ القرآن قد أوجب على المرأة المتزوجة، عند انحلال الزواج بالطلاق أن تتربص (أي تنتظر دون زواج جديد مدة ثلاثة أدوار طمثية إن كانت تحيض، أو ثلاثة أشهر إن كانت لا تحيض). وعند التأيم،

(1) كنهي النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن خطبة الإنسان على خطبة أخيه، أو سومه على سوم أخيه . - أخرجه البخاري (٥١٤٤) ، ومسلم : ۲ : ۱۰۲۹ (۳۸) ـ أي لا يجوز لأحد، إذا رأى غيره يخطب امرأة للزواج، أو يساوم بائعاً على شيء ليشتريه منه، أن يأتي هو فيزاحمه على الخطبة أو الشراء، بل عليه أن ينتظر ، فإذا لم يتم الاتفاق بين الطرفين تقدم هو للطلب .

(1) كنهي النبي عليه السلام عن بيع الغَرَر (بفتحتين)، قال ابن الأثير في «جامع الأصول» ٥٢٧/١ : الغرر ما له ظاهر تؤثره وباطن تكرهه فظاهره يغرُ المشتري، وباطنه مجهول) انتهى. فبيع الأشياء الاحتمالية غير المحققة الوجود أو الحدود، منهي عنه لما فيه من مغامرة وتغرير يجعله أشبه بالقمار كبيع ضربة القانص أو الغائص، أي ما ستخرجه شبكة الصياد من سمك، أو غوصة الغواص من لؤلؤ . فهذا نص عام يدخل جميع أنواع الغرر وانظر ما سيأتي في معنى النص العام ف ٢/٧١). هذا القبيل، أي غير القطعي جميع النصوص العامة في القرآن أو في السنة النبوية في نظر معظم أئمة الفقه الإسلامي سوى الحنفية فإن النص العام هو في نظر الأئمة غير قطعي الدلالة بسبب عمومه وكذا نصوص الحديث النبوي الثابتة برواية الآحاد ولو بطرق صحيحة فإنها عندهم غير قطعية الثبوت بوجه عام، ولو كانت قطعية الدلالة على المعنى المراد . (2)
Chapter (5): Subsidiary Sources: Istislah

20/5 - Conflict of Mursal Interests with Shariah Texts:

We have previously seen in the definition of maslaha mursala that it is that which agrees with the general objectives of the Shariah without there being a Shariah text concerning it or anything similar to it such that it could be analogized to it.

So it is assumed, therefore, in matters and rulings that ijtihad in fiqh builds upon the principle of maslaha, that there is no Shariah text commanding them, or commanding something that shares a similar ratio legis (illa) with them such that they could be analogized to it; for if such a text existed on the subject, the desired ruling would be attributed to it or to the analogy based upon it, not to mere maslaha, which Islamic law has required to be observed in general (cf. §1/5).

But the opposite is conceivable and occurs, namely that a preventing Shariah text obstructs the path of a maslaha that agrees with the objectives of the Shariah. So in that case, does one act upon the text and ignore the maslaha, or upon the maslaha and ignore the text? What is the juristic position on that?

Indeed, Shariah texts are of two types:

Furthermore, a Shariah text may be definitive (qat'i) in its indication (dalala) of the intended meaning and in the certainty of its transmission (thubut) from the Lawgiver; and it may be non-definitive in one of these two aspects: either indication or transmission (2).

So what we deem to be a maslaha according to our own opinion while it contradicts a qat'i text is, in that case, a mafsada (source of harm) in the view of the Lawgiver from other preponderant aspects. There is no doubt about the necessity of acting upon the text and ignoring this illusory maslaha. This is agreed upon by the imams and jurists of the Shariah, except for some individual exceptions like Sulayman al-Tufi.

An example of that is that the Qur'an has obligated upon a married woman, upon dissolution of marriage by divorce, to observe an 'iddah (i.e., wait without new marriage) for a period of three menstrual cycles if she menstruates, or three months if she does not menstruate. And regarding the widow, ...

(1) Such as the Prophet's prohibition (peace be upon him) of a person proposing marriage over the proposal of his brother, or bargaining over the bargain of his brother. Reported by Bukhari (5144) and Muslim (2:1029, no. 38). That is, it is not permissible for anyone, if he sees another person proposing to a woman for marriage, or negotiating with a seller over something to buy from him, to come and crowd him in the proposal or purchase; rather, he must wait, and if the two parties do not reach an agreement, he may then come forward with his request.

(1) Such as the Prophet's prohibition (peace be upon him) of the sale of gharar (uncertainty). Ibn al-Athir said in Jam' al-Usul (1/527): "Gharar is that which has an appealing exterior and a disliked interior; its exterior deceives the buyer, and its interior is unknown." Therefore, selling probabilistic things whose existence or boundaries are not ascertained is prohibited because it involves risk and deception that makes it resemble gambling, such as selling the catch of a hunter or diver, i.e., whatever the fisherman's net brings out or the diver's dive brings up. This kind, i.e., non-definitive, includes all general texts in the Qur'an or in the Sunna according to most imams of Islamic fiqh except the Hanafis. For the general text is, in the view of the imams [of the majority], non-definitive in indication due to its generality; likewise, texts of prophetic hadith established through ahad (solitary) transmission, even if through authentic chains, are generally non-definitive in transmission in their view, even if they are definitive in indication of the intended meaning. (2)

Commentary
This passage is a legal-philosophical discussion on the nature of maslaha mursala (unrestricted public interest) as a subsidiary source of Islamic law. The passage then categorizes nusus into specific and general, and further divides them by certainty: qat'i (definitive) and zanni (speculative). The key ruling is that if a nass is qat'i in both its indication and transmission, no maslaha can override it, because what appears to us as a benefit but contradicts a definitive text is actually a harm (mafsada) from the divine perspective. المصلحة المرسلة (al-maslaha al-mursala): مصلحة لا يشهد لها نص شرعي بالاعتبار ولا بالإلغاء، ولكنها توافق مقاصد الشريعة العامة

النص العام (al-nass al-'amm): النص الذي يستغرق أفراداً كثيرة متجانسة بحكم واحد

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of a maslaha that contradicts a qat'i text?
A) It is a valid maslaha if it serves a greater good.
B) It is an illusory maslaha (mawhumah) and actually a mafsada.
C) It can be considered if the text is general.
D) It is a legitimate subject of ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
A qat'i text, whether specific or general (according to Hanafis), cannot be overridden by any maslaha; only zanni texts may be weighed against maslaha.

The Priority of Definitive Texts Over Maslaha
Explaining the priority of definitive texts and ijtihad differences for non-definitive texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between definitive (qat'i) and non-definitive (ghayr qat'i) texts and explain why a claimed maslaha cannot override a definitive text according to the Hanafi and majority positions.

Core Idea
A definitive text overrides any supposed maslaha; only non-definitive texts allow ijtihad on maslaha.

One of the most critical tools in the mufti's methodology is knowing when a text can be weighed against public interest (maslaha). This lesson clarifies the absolute priority of definitive texts—those certain in transmission and meaning—and explains why any alleged maslaha opposing such a text is legally void. It also introduces the scholarly disagreement over general texts (al-‘amm), marking the boundary where ijtihad begins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text's classification
Determine whether the text is definitive (qat'i) in both transmission and meaning, or non-definitive in one aspect. This classification dictates whether maslaha can even be considered.
2
Apply the rule for definitive texts
For qat'i texts, any maslaha that contradicts the text is automatically invalid—it is actually a mafsada. Accept this as a settled principle across the schools except for fringe views.
3
Examine the example: 'iddah rulings
The Qur'anic verses on 'iddah are cited as an example of a qat'i text. Even if one imagines a benefit in shortening the waiting period, the text prevails because the Lawgiver sees a greater harm.
4
Understand the dispute over general texts
Most scholars (Shafi'is, Malikis, etc.) consider general texts as non-definitive in indication due to their generality. Hanafis hold a different view, which will be detailed in the dispute map.
This dispute sets the stage for the second section on non-definitive texts.

ثم إنَّ النص الشرعي قد يكون قطعياً في دلالته على المعنى المراد، وفي ثبوت نقله عن الشارع ؛ وقد يكون غير قطعي في إحدى هاتين الجهتين: أي الدلالة، أو الثبوت.
٢١/٥ - أ - المصلحة تجاه النص القطعي :
فإذا كان النص قطعياً في دلالته وثبوته لا يتصور أن تعارضه مصلحة تقتضي خلافه، لأن معيار المصلحة هو النظر الشرعي.
فما نظنه مصلحة بنظرنا الخاص وهو معارض لنص قطعي هو عندئذ مفسدة في نظر الشارع من وجوه أخرى راجحة فلا شك في لزوم العمل بالنص دون هذه المصلحة الموهومة وهذا مُتَّفق عليه بين أئمة فقهاء الشريعة، إلا بعض شذوذات فردية من أناس كسليمان الطوفي.
مثال ذلك أنَّ القرآن قد أوجب على المرأة المتزوجة، عند انحلال الزواج بالطلاق أن تتربص (أي تنتظر دون زواج جديد) مدة ثلاثة أدوار طمثية إن كانت تحيض، أو ثلاثة أشهر إن كانت لا تحيض. وعند التأيم، أي انحلال الزواج بوفاة الزوج، أوجب عليها أن تتربص كذلك أربعة أشهر وعشرة أيام. وإذا كانت المرأة حاملاً فعدتها تمتد حتى وضع الحمل في جميع الأحوال. وذلك لاعتبارات شرعية أهمها صيانة الأنساب من الضياع بالاختلاط؛ لأن المرأة إذا تزوجت إثر انحلال الزواج السابق ثم ظهر بها حمل فإنه لا يعرف من أي الزوجين هو؟ فهذا نص قطعي الدلالة والثبوت في وجوب العدة. فمهما تصور أحد مصلحة في إهمال العدة أو في نقص مدتها لا ينهض ذلك حجة في وجه هذا النص القاطع، ولا يصح زواج المرأة قبل انقضاء عدتها، لأنَّ مراد الشارع واضح كل الوضوح من النص، وهو لم يهمل اعتبار المصلحة التي نتصورها في الموضوع إلا لأنه يرى في مقابلها مفسدة أعظم منها . وقد قدَّمنا أن كل أمر فيه جهتا نفع وضرر، وإنما العبرة للجهة الراجحة (ر : ف ٥/٥).
(1) كنهي النبي عليه السلام عن بيع الغَرَر (بفتحتين)، قال ابن الأثير في جامع الأصول» ٥٢٧/١ : الغرر ما له ظاهر تؤثره وباطن تكرهه فظاهره يغرُ المشتري، وباطنه مجهول) انتهى. فبيع الأشياء الاحتمالية غير المحققة الوجود أو الحدود، منهي عنه لما فيه من مغامرة وتغرير يجعله أشبه بالقمار كبيع ضربة القانص أو الغائص، أي ما ستخرجه شبكة الصياد من سمك، أو غوصة الغواص من لؤلؤ . فهذا نص عام يدخل جميع أنواع الغرر. وانظر ما سيأتي في معنى النص العام ف ٢/٧١). هذا القبيل، أي غير القطعي جميع النصوص العامة في القرآن أو في السنة النبوية في نظر معظم أئمة الفقه الإسلامي سوى الحنفية فإن النص العام هو في نظر الأئمة غير قطعي الدلالة بسبب عمومه وكذا نصوص الحديث النبوي الثابتة برواية الآحاد ولو بطرق صحيحة فإنها عندهم غير قطعية الثبوت بوجه عام، ولو كانت قطعية الدلالة على المعنى المراد .
٢٢/٥ - ب - المصلحة تجاه النص غير القطعي :
أما إذا كان النص غير قطعي في دلالته أو ثبوته فإن الاجتهادات مختلفة في جواز تقييده وتخصيصه بالمصلحة عند التعارض :

لكن إذا اعترض سبيل تطبيق النص ضرر عارض فعندئذ تحكم قاعدة الضرورات، واختيار أهون الشرين فإنَّ الضرورات تبيح المحظورات.

Second Chapter: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence
And many homogeneous situations and individuals (1)
Then, the legal text may be definitive in its indication of the intended meaning and in the certainty of its transmission from the Lawgiver; or it may be non-definitive in one of these two aspects: either indication or transmission.
21/5 - A - Maslaha in the face of a definitive text:
If the text is definitive in its indication and transmission, it is inconceivable that a maslaha requiring the opposite would oppose it, because the criterion of maslaha is the Shari'a perspective.
What we consider a maslaha by our own opinion and which contradicts a definitive text is then a mafsada from the Shari'a perspective due to other preponderant aspects, so there is no doubt about the necessity of acting on the text without this illusory maslaha. This is agreed upon among the jurist imams of the Shari'a, except for some individual eccentricities like those of Sulayman al-Tufi.
An example of that is that the Qur'an has required of a married woman, upon dissolution of marriage by divorce, to wait (i.e., not marry anew) for three menstrual periods if she menstruates, or three months if she does not menstruate. And upon widowhood, i.e., dissolution of marriage by the husband's death, it required her to wait likewise for four months and ten days. And if the woman is pregnant, her 'iddah extends until delivery in all cases. That is due to legal considerations, the most important being the preservation of lineages from loss through mixing; because if a woman marries immediately after the dissolution of the previous marriage and then becomes pregnant, it will not be known which husband is the father. So this is a text definitive in indication and transmission regarding the obligation of the 'iddah. No matter how one imagines a maslaha in neglecting the 'iddah or reducing its duration, that does not stand as proof against this definitive text. It is not valid for a woman to marry before the completion of her 'iddah, because the intent of the Lawgiver is completely clear from the text, and He did not neglect the consideration of the maslaha we imagine in the matter except because He sees a greater mafsaha in opposition to it. And we have already presented that every matter has two sides of benefit and harm, and consideration is given to the preponderant side (see: 5/5).
(1) Like the Prophet's prohibition of selling gharar (with two fathas). Ibn al-Athir said in Jami' al-Usul (1/527): 'Gharar is what has an appealing exterior and a detestable interior; its exterior entices the buyer, its interior is unknown.' End quote. So selling probabilistic things whose existence or limits are not realized is prohibited because it involves risk and deception, making it akin to gambling, like selling the catch of a hunter or a diver, i.e., what the fisherman's net will bring out or the diver's plunge will yield of pearls. So this is a general text that includes all types of gharar. And see what will come on the meaning of the general text in 2/71). This kind, i.e., non-definitive, all general texts in the Qur'an or in the Prophetic Sunnah according to most imams of Islamic jurisprudence except the Hanafis, for the general text is in the view of the imams non-definitive in indication due to its generality, and likewise texts of prophetic hadith established through ahad narration, even if authentic chains, are in their view generically non-definitive in transmission, even if definitive in indication of the intended meaning.
22/5 - B - Maslaha in the face of a non-definitive text:
As for when the text is non-definitive in its indication or transmission, the ijtihads differ regarding the permissibility of restricting and specifying it by maslaha when there is conflict:
1 - The ijtihads that condemn the theories of istihsan and istislah and reject them, such as the Shafi'i ijtihad, do not accept the specification of the text - even if non-definitive - by maslaha, because one who rejects the authority of unrestricted maslaha in the absence of a text rejects it a fortiori when it opposes a text.
But if a contingent harm impedes the application of the text, then the rule of necessities applies, and choosing the lesser of two evils, for necessities permit prohibitions.
Imam al-Ghazali is of the opinion in this context that if contingent circumstances arise such that maslaha requires contravening the legal text, and adhering to it would result in...
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm discusses the relationship between maslaha (public interest) and legal texts. It begins by classifying texts as definitive (qat'i) in both indication and transmission, or non-definitive in one aspect. The author then presents two cases. In the first case (section A), when a text is definitive, no claimed maslaha can override it, because the true measure of maslaha is the Shari'a itself. Any supposed benefit contradicting a definitive text is actually a harm (mafsada) from the divine perspective. The author illustrates this with the Qur'anic rulings on 'iddah (waiting period) for divorced and widowed women, emphasizing that even if someone imagines a benefit in shortening or ignoring the 'iddah, the text takes precedence because the Lawgiver sees a greater harm in doing so. The footnote attached to the first paragraph clarifies the concept of gharar (uncertainty) as an example of a general text, and notes that according to most scholars (except Hanafis), general texts are non-definitive in indication. In the second case (section B, incomplete in this window), the author addresses non-definitive texts. Here, ijtihad differs: the Shafi'i school, which rejects istihsan and istislah, does not allow restricting even a non-definitive text by maslaha, except when necessity (darura) arises. Al-Ghazali's view, which begins to be mentioned, presumably allows consideration of maslaha under certain conditions. The discussion cuts off, indicating the need to consult the complete text.

Key Terms
نص قطعي (nass qat'i): A text that is definitive in both its meaning (dalala) and its transmission (thubut) from the Lawgiver
مصلحة (maslaha): Public interest or benefit that aligns with the objectives of the Shari'a
استصلاح (istislah): The method of deriving rulings based on unrestricted maslaha (maslaha mursala) not explicitly mentioned in the sources

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the status of a general text (al-‘amm) in the view of the majority of Islamic jurists?
A) It is definitive in indication because it is from the Qur'an or authentic hadith.
B) It is non-definitive in indication due to its generality.
C) It is non-definitive in transmission but definitive in indication.
D) It is definitive in both indication and transmission.

Key Takeaway
A definitive text cannot be overridden by any claimed maslaha; only non-definitive texts allow ijtihad where maslaha may be considered, under specific conditions.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
8 min
Definitive Text (al-Nass al-Qat'i) Cannot Be Overridden by Maslahah
Definitive text vs maslahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a definitive text (qat'i) cannot be set aside by a claimed maslahah, and identify the principle of darurah as the only exception.

Core Idea
A definitive text (qat'i) prevails over any speculative maslahah; only necessity (darurah) can permit violation.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule in usul al-fiqh: a text that is definitive in both transmission and meaning is immune to being overridden by considerations of public interest (maslahah). Using the example of the iddah (waiting period) for widows, the author shows that even a seemingly beneficial goal cannot outweigh a clear command of the Lawgiver. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti to avoid unjustified departures from established rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitive text
The text concerning the iddah of a widow: four months and ten days, or until delivery if pregnant. This is based on Qur'an 2:234 and 2:228, which are qat'i al-thubut wa al-dalalah.
The text is both definitively transmitted and unequivocal in meaning.
2
Recognize the strength of the text
The author states: 'So this is a text that is definitive in its indication and transmission regarding obligation.' This means no ijtihad can alter it.
A qat'i text is binding and not open to interpretation.
3
Consider the hypothetical maslahah
One might imagine a maslahah in shortening or abolishing the iddah, e.g., to facilitate remarriage or reduce hardship.
The author calls this a 'speculative' maslahah.
4
Apply the principle that the Lawgiver has already weighed the harms and benefits
The author explains that the Lawgiver did not consider the imagined maslahah because it would lead to a greater harm (loss of lineage). Thus, the qat'i text cannot be overridden.
The principle: every matter has two aspects; the preponderant one prevails.
5
Note the only exception: darurah (necessity)
While no ordinary maslahah can override a qat'i text, a situation of extreme necessity (darurah) may permit violation under the principle of choosing the lesser of two harms. This is not based on maslahah mursalah but on necessity.
This exception is agreed upon by all schools.

الفصل (٥) المصادر التبعية : الاستصلاح
أي انحلال الزواج بوفاة الزوج، أوجب عليها أن تتربص كذلك أربعة أشهر وعشرة أيام. وإذا كانت المرأة حاملاً فعدتها تمتد حتى وضع الحمل في جميع الأحوال. وذلك لاعتبارات شرعية أهمها صيانة الأنساب من الضياع بالاختلاط؛ لأن المرأة إذا تزوجت إثر انحلال الزواج السابق ثم ظهر بها حمل فإنه لا يعرف من أي الزوجين هو؟ فهذا نص قطعي الدلالة والثبوت في وجوب وفي فمهما تصور أحد مصلحة في إهمال العدة أو في نقص مدتها لا من ينهض ذلك حجة في وجه هذا النص القاطع، ولا يصح زواج المرأة قبل انقضاء عدتها، لأنَّ مراد الشارع واضح كل الوضوح من النص، وهو لم يهمل اعتبار المصلحة التي نتصورها في الموضوع إلا لأنه يرى في مقابلها مفسدة أعظم منها . وقد قدَّمنا أن كل أمر فيه جهتا نفع وضرر، وإنما العبرة للجهة الراجحة (ر : ف ٥/٥).
