فأبقى عمر الأرضين لأهليها، وطرح عليها ضريبة الخراج؛ لأن ذلك أصلح لإحيائها وأعم وأدوم لنفعها وريعها (1).
هذا، وإن عمر هو أول أنشأ منصب القضاء مستقلاً من عن غيره من الأعمال، وكان قبل ذلك تابعاً لولاية الأمراء والعمال، ومن جملة وظائفهم.
وإن طريقة عمر الفقهية كانت حجة خالدة لمدرسة «أهل الرأي» في العراق من فقهاء الطبقات التالية التي سيأتي ذكرها فقد تأثر هؤلاء بفقه ابن مسعود في الكوفة، وكان هو يسير على طريقة عمر رضي الله عنهما.
(۱) روي من حديث عائشة، ومن حديث علي ومن حديث أبي هريرة، أما حديث عائشة فأخرجه الترمذي (١٤٢٤) في الحدود، بلفظ: ادرؤوا الحدود عن المسلمين ما استطعتم فإن كان له مخرج فخلوا سبيله، فإن الإمام أن يخطىء في العفو خير من يخطىء في العقوبة وضعف رفعه وأخرجه الحاكم في المستدرك ٣٨٤/٤، وقال: صحيح الإسناد، وتعقبه الذهبي. وأما حديث علي فأخرجه الدارقطني ٨٤/٣ وأما حديث أبي هريرة فأخرجه ابن ماجه (٢٥٤٥) بلفظ : ادفعوا الحدود ما وجدتم له مدفعاً». وأخرجه ابن عدي في جزء له عن ابن عباس مرفوعاً بلفظ : ادرؤوا الحدود بالشبهات وأقيلوا الكرام عثراتهم إلا في حد من حدود الله» (ر:ف ٤/٤٩).
(۱) فصلنا اجتهاد عمر في شأن الأراضي المفتوحة في الملحق بهذا الفصل.
Chapter (11) Second Cycle: The Era of the Rightly Guided Caliphs
2 - Likewise, Umar's ijtihad in suspending the execution of the hadd punishment for theft on thieves in the year of famine called (Year of Ramadah); and his sufficing with tazir (discretionary punishment) for the thief instead of cutting off his hand. This from Umar is not a suspension of the legal hadd for theft, but is a wise ijtihad from him in applying the conditions of this punishment, because among its conditions legally is that the thief not be compelled to theft by necessity. So Umar considered in that a general doubt (shubha) that they were stealing due to compelling necessity, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Avert the hudud by doubts (shubuhat).' (1)
3 - Likewise, his permitting marriage for the wife of a missing person after four years of his disappearance without waiting for verification of his death or the death of his peers - i.e., his age mates - as previously mentioned in the discussion of considerations of public interest (masalih mursalah). (See: f 12/5).
4 - Likewise, Umar's ijtihad in preventing the division of the lands of Sawad of Iraq and the lands of Egypt among the conquering mujahideen who demanded their division among themselves as war booty is divided, after taking one-fifth, arguing with the apparent meanings of some Quranic and Sunnah texts regarding the rights of mujahideen to spoils; for they intended to consider the lands of the conquered territories as war booty distributed to the conquering army.
And Umar went contrary to their opinion, and he considered the lands as fay' (public property) to which the rights of Muslims in general, present and future, are attached, taking care of the interest of generations and their rights in the treasury, according to what sound consideration of the totality of Quranic texts indicates, not some of them without others.
So Umar left the lands to their owners, and imposed upon them the kharaj tax; because that was more beneficial for their cultivation and more comprehensive and lasting for their benefit and yield (1).
Moreover, Umar was the first to establish the position of judiciary independently from other offices, whereas before it was subordinate to the governors and officials, and part of their functions.
And indeed, Umar's jurisprudential method was an enduring proof for the school of 'Ahl al-Ra'y' in Iraq among the jurists of the following generations who will be mentioned later; for these were influenced by the fiqh of Ibn Mas'ud in Kufa, and he followed the method of Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both).
(1) Narrated from the hadith of Aisha, and from the hadith of Ali, and from the hadith of Abu Hurairah. As for the hadith of Aisha, it is recorded by al-Tirmidhi (1424) in the Book of Hudud with the wording: 'Avert the hudud from the Muslims as much as you can; if there is a way out, let him go, for the Imam to err in pardon is better than to err in punishment.' And he considered its raising (to the Prophet) weak. Al-Hakim recorded it in al-Mustadrak (4/384) and said: 'The chain is authentic,' but al-Dhahabi criticized it. As for the hadith of Ali, it is recorded by al-Daraqutni (3/84). As for the hadith of Abu Hurairah, it is recorded by Ibn Majah (2545) with the wording: 'Avert the hudud as long as you find a way to avert them.' And Ibn Adi recorded in a part of his work from Ibn Abbas with a raised chain: 'Avert the hudud by doubts and overlook the slips of the noble except in a hadd from the limits of Allah.' (See: f 4/49).
(1) We have detailed Umar's ijtihad regarding the conquered lands in the appendix to this chapter.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's work presents a historical and legal analysis of three famous ijtihadat of Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA). The author classifies this as part of the 'second cycle' of Islamic jurisprudence: the era of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The passage serves to illustrate how early juristic reasoning (ijtihad) operated within the framework of Sharia by applying general principles and conditions rather than merely following literal texts.

The first example concerns the suspension of the hadd punishment for theft during the severe famine known as 'Year of Ramadah.' Umar refrained from amputating thieves' hands and instead imposed a lesser discretionary punishment (ta'zir). The author clarifies that this was not an abandonment of the divine penalty but a proper application of its conditions: one condition is that the thief not be compelled by necessity. Umar considered the widespread famine as creating a general doubt (shubha) about criminal intent, relying on the Prophetic instruction to avert hudud by doubts. This demonstrates ijtihad based on textual evidence (the hadith) and causal reasoning ('illa).

The second example is Umar's ruling on the wife of a missing person. He allowed her to remarry after four years of waiting, without requiring proof of death or waiting for her husband's age-peers to die. The author references this as an application of masalih mursalah (considerations of public interest), a principle accepted by the Hanafi school. This shows ijtihad based on broader social welfare.

The third and most detailed example concerns the conquered lands of Iraq and Egypt. The conquering soldiers demanded distribution as war booty (ghanimah), citing Quranic verses about spoils. Umar disagreed, classifying the lands as fay' (public property) belonging to the entire Muslim community, present and future. He based this on a comprehensive reading of Quranic texts and the public interest of maintaining agricultural productivity and revenue for the treasury. He imposed kharaj tax on the original owners, keeping the lands productive.

The passage concludes by noting that Umar established the judiciary as an independent institution, and that his jurisprudential method became the model for the 'Ahl al-Ra'y' (School of Opinion) in Iraq, which later influenced the Hanafi school through Ibn Mas'ud and his students.

Key Terms
أهل الرأي (Ahl al-Ra'y): The 'School of Opinion' in early Islamic jurisprudence, known for using reasoned opinion and analogy.
قضاء (qada'): The judicial function; the position of a judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, whose fiqh did the Ahl al-Ra'y jurists in Kufa follow as a link to Umar?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Ibn Mas'ud
C) Zayd ibn Thabit
D) Ali ibn Abi Talib

Key Takeaway
Umar's ijtihad established a methodology of reasoned legal interpretation that became the foundation of the Hanafi school.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
10 min
Umar's Ijtihad: Synthesizing Ghanimah and Fay'
Textual analysis of Umar's ijtihad on land distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze Caliph Umar's ijtihad on conquered lands by identifying the Quranic verses of ghanimah and fay', distinguishing their respective scopes, and deriving the ruling that such lands are fay' not ghanimah.

Core Idea
Land conquered without direct war is fay' for all Muslims, not ghanimah for fighters.

This lesson examines the pivotal ijtihad of Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab regarding the conquered lands of Sawad (Iraq) and Egypt. Facing the question of whether to distribute these lands as war spoils (ghanimah) among the soldiers, Umar chose instead to leave them with their original owners and impose the kharaj tax. This decision was not arbitrary; it was rooted in a comprehensive understanding of two key Quranic verses: the verse of spoils (Surah al-Anfal 8:41) and the verse of fay' (Surah al-Hashr 59:7-10). By synthesizing these texts, Umar established that land, as immovable property acquired without direct combat, falls under the category of fay', which benefits the entire Muslim community across generations. This lesson walks through the textual evidence and Umar's legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Quranic Texts
Read the verse of ghanimah (8:41) and the verse of fay' (59:7-10) as quoted in the source. Note their different contexts: ghanimah refers to movable spoils taken in battle, while fay' refers to property acquired from non-Muslims without warfare, such as lands surrendered peacefully.
The key Arabic terms are غَنِمْتُم (you take as spoils) and أَفَاءَ (He restored/caused to return).
2
Distinguish the Allocation Rules
According to the ghanimah verse, one-fifth is allocated to public purposes and the remainder is distributed among the fighters. The fay' verse, however, specifies that it is for Allah, the Messenger, relatives, orphans, needy, and traveler—and crucially, it includes 'those who come after them' (Surah al-Hashr 59:10), indicating an ongoing public benefit.
The phrase 'so that it does not become a circulation among the rich' (59:7) reinforces the public ownership aspect.
3
Map Umar's Ijtihad onto the Texts
Umar reasoned that the conquered lands of Sawad and Egypt were acquired without direct military assault? They were taken by treaty or after resistance but were not subject to the standard distribution of ghanimah. Therefore, they fell under the ruling of fay', meaning they become a permanent endowment for the Muslim community, to be administered for public benefit.
The author notes that this was based on 'sound consideration of the totality of Quranic texts' (النظر السديد إلى مجموع النصوص القرآنية).
4
Identify the Practical Outcome
The practical result was that the lands remained with their original owners (mostly Zoroastrian farmers) who paid kharaj tax, ensuring continuous agricultural production and a steady revenue stream for the state treasury (Bayt al-Mal). This prevented the land from being monopolized by a few wealthy soldiers.
The kharaj is a land tax distinct from jizya; it is tied to the land’s productivity.

Supplement to Chapter Eleven
'Umar's Ijtihad Concerning Conquered Lands
11/5 - We explained in Chapter 11 that 'Umar's ijtihad was not to divide the lands of Sawad of Iraq and the lands of Egypt among the conquerors as war spoils are divided. Below is an explanation of that:
Indeed, the verse of spoils came in Surat al-Anfal saying: 'And know that whatever you take as spoils of war, then indeed, for Allah is one fifth of it and for the Messenger and for the near relative and the orphans and the needy and the traveler' (8:41).
So the verse specified the expenditure of one-fifth of war spoils for public purposes, and the Sunnah by the practice of the Prophet, peace be upon him, explained the method of distributing the remainder among the conquerors.
Then came the verse of fay' in Surat al-Hashr saying: 'What Allah has restored to His Messenger from the people of the towns - it is for Allah and for the Messenger and for the near relative and the orphans and the needy and the traveler, so that it does not become a circulation among the rich from among you. And whatever the Messenger has given you - take; and whatever he has forbidden you - refrain from. And fear Allah; indeed, Allah is severe in penalty. For the poor emigrants who were expelled from their homes... and those who settled in the city and [adopted] the faith before them... and those who come after them.'
So this verse indicated that fay' benefits all Muslims, present and future, and is not exclusive to the conquering mujahideen, but rather is placed in the public treasury.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a historical and legal analysis of Caliph Umar's ijtihad regarding conquered lands. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, presents this as part of a broader discussion on the stages of Islamic fiqh development. The key point is that Umar did not distribute the agricultural lands of Iraq and Egypt as spoils of war among the soldiers, but instead left them with the original owners and imposed the kharaj tax. The author argues that this was based on a holistic reading of Quranic texts, considering both the ayah of ghanimah (spoils) in Surah al-Anfal and the ayah of fay' in Surah al-Hashr. The former deals with movable spoils, where the Prophet distributed four-fifths among the fighters; the latter deals with land and immovable property acquired without direct fighting, which the Quran designates for the entire Muslim community, not just the fighters. Umar's ijtihad became a foundational precedent for the 'Ahl al-Ra'y' school in Iraq, particularly through the influence of Ibn Mas'ud in Kufa. The passage also highlights Umar's role in establishing the judiciary as an independent institution. This analysis is significant in Hanafi usul al-iftah because it shows how a companion's ijtihad, based on maslahah and textual synthesis, shaped later juristic methodology.

Key Terms
الفيء (al-fay'): Property acquired from non-Muslims without warfare, which according to the Quran is for the benefit of all Muslims and placed in the public treasury.
الخراج (al-kharaj): A land tax imposed on non-Muslim landowners of conquered territories in lieu of jizya or as a rental for the land that remains in their possession.
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): Spoils of war obtained from fighting, which are distributed among the soldiers after deducting one-fifth for public purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate

Umar's Method as the Foundation of Ahl al-Ra'y
Historical analysis of Umar's juristic method and its transmission to Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Umar's ijtihad on conquered lands established the methodological approach of Ahl al-Ra'y and how this lineage influenced Hanafi usul al-iftah.

Core Idea
Umar's rational synthesis of texts became the prototype for Hanafi reliance on ra'y and maslahah.

In the previous lesson, we analyzed Umar's specific ijtihad on land. Now we explore its broader legacy. The source passage states that 'Umar's juristic method was an eternal proof for the school of Ahl al-Ra'y in Iraq.' This lesson traces how Umar's approach—holistic reading of texts, consideration of public interest, and independent reasoning—was transmitted through Ibn Mas'ud in Kufa and became the hallmark of the Hanafi school. Understanding this lineage is crucial for a mufti, as it legitimizes the use of ra'y and istihsan in deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify Umar's Juristic Method
The source describes Umar's method as 'sound consideration of the totality of Quranic texts' (النظر السديد إلى مجموع النصوص القرآنية). This means not taking one verse in isolation but synthesizing all relevant texts. It also involved considering maslahah (public benefit), as seen in his reasoning that leaving land with its owners was 'more suitable for cultivation and more lasting for benefit.'
This is the essence of what later became known as ra'y—reasoned opinion based on textual foundations.
2
Trace the Transmission Chain
The author explicitly links Umar's method to Ibn Mas'ud in Kufa, who was a student of Umar. Ibn Mas'ud's fiqh then became the foundation of the Kufan school, which developed into the Ahl al-Ra'y. This chain legitimizes the Hanafi school's methodological principles.
The chain: Umar → Ibn Mas'ud → Ahl al-Ra'y (including Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman) → Abu Hanifa.
3
Understand the Concept of Ahl al-Ra'y
Ahl al-Ra'y refers to the jurists who, while relying on the Quran and Sunnah, also employed analogical reasoning (qiyas) and considered public interest (maslahah) when the texts were silent or ambiguous. This contrasts with Ahl al-Hadith, who relied more heavily on transmitted reports.
The term is not derogatory; it signifies a balanced methodology.
4
Apply the Legacy to Modern Iftaa
A mufti trained in the Hanafi tradition can, following Umar's model, consider the overall objectives of shariah (maqasid) and the current context when issuing fatwas. The precedent of Umar allows for flexibility within textual boundaries.
Umar's ijtihad is not just historical; it is a living methodological precedent.

ثم جاءت آية الفيء في سورة الحشر تقول:
لوما
ما أَفَاءَ اللهُ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْقُرَى فَلِلَّهِ وَلِلرَّسُولِ وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى وَالْيَتَمَى وَالْمَسَكِينِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ كَي لَا يَكُونَ دُولَةٌ بَيْنَ الْأَغْنِيَاءِ مِنكُمْ وَمَا الَكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ وَمَا نَهَنكُمْ عَنْهُ فَانتَهُوا وَاتَّقُوا اللهَ إِنَّ اللَّهَ شَدِيدُ الْعِقَابِ * لِلْفُقَرَاءِ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ الَّذِينَ أُخْرِجُوا مِن دِيَارِهِمْ
وَالَّذِينَ تَبَوَّهُ وَ الدَّارَ وَالْإِيمَنَ مِن قَبْلِهِمْ ... وَالَّذِينَ جَاءُو مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ ٢٠٠٠
.
فأفادت هذه الآية أنَّ الفيء يفيد منه جميع المسلمين حاضرهم وآتيهم
ولا يختص بالمجاهدين الفاتحين بل يوضع في بيت المال.
Chapter Three: Stages of Development of Islamic Fiqh and Its Characteristics
And its rights in the public treasury, according to what sound consideration of the totality of Quranic texts indicates, not some of them to the exclusion of others.
So 'Umar left the lands with their people and imposed upon them the tax of kharaj, because that was more suitable for their cultivation and more general and lasting for their benefit and yield (1).
Moreover, 'Umar was the first to establish the judiciary as an independent office separate from other functions, whereas before it was subordinate to the governance of amirs and officials and part of their duties.
And indeed 'Umar's juristic method was an eternal proof for the school of 'Ahl al-Ra'y' in Iraq among the jurists of the subsequent generations that will be mentioned; for they were influenced by the fiqh of Ibn Mas'ud in Kufa, and he followed the method of 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both.
(1) We have detailed 'Umar's ijtihad concerning conquered lands in the supplement to this chapter.

Supplement to Chapter Eleven
'Umar's Ijtihad Concerning Conquered Lands
11/5 - We explained in Chapter 11 that 'Umar's ijtihad was not to divide the lands of Sawad of Iraq and the lands of Egypt among the conquerors as war spoils are divided. Below is an explanation of that:
Indeed, the verse of spoils came in Surat al-Anfal saying: 'And know that whatever you take as spoils of war, then indeed, for Allah is one fifth of it and for the Messenger and for the near relative and the orphans and the needy and the traveler' (8:41).
So the verse specified the expenditure of one-fifth of war spoils for public purposes, and the Sunnah by the practice of the Prophet, peace be upon him, explained the method of distributing the remainder among the conquerors.
Then came the verse of fay' in Surat al-Hashr saying: 'What Allah has restored to His Messenger from the people of the towns - it is for Allah and for the Messenger and for the near relative and the orphans and the needy and the traveler, so that it does not become a circulation among the rich from among you. And whatever the Messenger has given you - take; and whatever he has forbidden you - refrain from. And fear Allah; indeed, Allah is severe in penalty. For the poor emigrants who were expelled from their homes... and those who settled in the city and [adopted] the faith before them... and those who come after them.'
So this verse indicated that fay' benefits all Muslims, present and future, and is not exclusive to the conquering mujahideen, but rather is placed in the public treasury.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a historical and legal analysis of Caliph Umar's ijtihad regarding conquered lands. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, presents this as part of a broader discussion on the stages of Islamic fiqh development. The key point is that Umar did not distribute the agricultural lands of Iraq and Egypt as spoils of war among the soldiers, but instead left them with the original owners and imposed the kharaj tax. The author argues that this was based on a holistic reading of Quranic texts, considering both the ayah of ghanimah (spoils) in Surah al-Anfal and the ayah of fay' in Surah al-Hashr. The former deals with movable spoils, where the Prophet distributed four-fifths among the fighters; the latter deals with land and immovable property acquired without direct fighting, which the Quran designates for the entire Muslim community, not just the fighters. Umar's ijtihad became a foundational precedent for the 'Ahl al-Ra'y' school in Iraq, particularly through the influence of Ibn Mas'ud in Kufa. The passage also highlights Umar's role in establishing the judiciary as an independent institution. This analysis is significant in Hanafi usul al-iftah because it shows how a companion's ijtihad, based on maslahah and textual synthesis, shaped later juristic methodology.

Key Terms
أهل الرأي (Ahl al-Ra'y): The school of Islamic jurisprudence that emphasizes reason and analogical reasoning (qiyas) alongside textual evidence, centered in Kufa and associated with Abu Hanifa and his predecessors such as Ibn Mas'ud and Umar.
طريقة عمر الفقهية (Tariqat Umar al-Fiqhiyya): The juristic method of Caliph Umar, characterized by holistic reading of texts, consideration of public benefit, and independent reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Whose fiqh did the Kufan school (Ahl al-Ra'y) follow, according to the passage?
A) Abu Hanifa directly
B) Ibn Mas'ud, who followed Umar's method
C) Ali ibn Abi Talib
D) Aisha

Key Takeaway
Umar's juristic method—synthesizing texts and considering maslahah—was transmitted through Ibn Mas'ud to the Ahl al-Ra'y school, forming the methodological backbone of Hanafi usul al-iftah.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
8 min
Distinction Between Ghanimah and Fay' and Umar's Ijtihad on Conquered Lands
Historical-legal analysis of ghanimah vs fay' with Caliph Umar's ruling on conquered lands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ghanimah and fay' in Hanafi fiqh, explain Umar's ijtihad on conquered lands, and evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah) of the Hanafi vs Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
Lands conquered by force are fay' not ghanimah: Umar's Quranic proof ensures perpetual benefit for the entire Muslim community.

This lesson explores one of the most significant ijtihads in Islamic legal history: Caliph Umar's decision not to distribute the conquered lands of Iraq as war booty. The passage first defines two key terms—ghanimah and fay'—then recounts the debate and Umar's reliance on Surah al-Hashr. Understanding this episode is essential for grasping the Hanafi position on land ownership and the role of maslahah in ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the definitions
Break down ghanimah and fay' by cause and legal effect: ghanimah is taken by force of arms and distributed after khums; fay' is acquired without direct combat and belongs to the community.
Pay attention to the element of 'iijaf al-khayl' (galloping horses) as a key differentiator.
2
Analyze the Prophetic precedent in Khaybar
The Prophet treated Khaybar lands as fay', setting aside part for public needs and dividing the rest. This shows that even conquered lands can be handled flexibly.
The Prophet's division was for a specific maslahah at that time.
3
Examine Umar's ijtihad
Umar refused to divide the Sawad lands, arguing they are fay'. His proof was the last verse of Surah al-Hashr, which includes future generations in the entitlement to fay'.
Umar's consultation with the Companions shows the collective ijtihad process.
4
Identify the opposing view
The Shafi'i school analogizes conquered lands to movable ghanimah, citing the Prophet's Khaybar precedent as a general rule.
The Hanafi response distinguishes the specific case from the general principle.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi → lands stay with original owners with kharaj; Shafi'i → lands become private property of conquerors after khums.
This affects tax policy and long-term community benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: أدوار تطور الفقه الإسلامي ومميزاته والفرق بين الغنيمة والفيء في الاصطلاح الشرعي أن الغنيمة ما استخلصت من العدو المحارب بقوة السلاح، والفيء ما تركه الأعداء عن رعب، أو أدوه عن قهر وغلبة ولم يؤخذ منهم بإيجاف الخيل وصولة الجيش في المعارك الحربية فيشمل الفيء الضرائب التي تفرض عليهم كالجزية على الأشخاص، والخراج على الأراضي.

وقد ثبت في السنة أنه عندما فتح النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام خيبر وقد فتحت عنوة لا صلحاً، ونزل أهلها المحاربون على حكم الجلاء - عُدَّت أراضيها من الفيء وعزل النبي نصفها (وقيل خمسها)، فتركه للنوائب والنوازل، وقسم الباقي بين الفاتحين.

فلما فتح سواد العراق في خلافة عمر طالب الفاتحون بتقسيم أراضيه بينهم كالغنائم، وكان رأي عمر عدم جواز تقسيمها، فجمع الناس واستشارهم. فكان رأي عامتهم تقسيمها إلا علياً وعثمان وطلحة ومعاذ بن جبل، فقد كان رأيهم كرأي عمر. وقال له معاذ : إنك إن قسمتها صار الريع العظيم في أيدي هؤلاء القوم. ثم يبيدون فيصير ذلك إلى الرجل الواحد أو المرأة ثم يأتي من بعدهم قوم يسدون من الإسلام مسدّاً ـ أي يكون لهم في الإسلام بلاء حسن ونفع . وهم لا يجدون شيئاً، فانظر أمراً يسع أولهم وآخرهم». فالح الفاتحون في طلب تقسيم الأرضين عليهم بعد تخميسها، بحجة ما فعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بخيبر، وامتنع عمر عن تقسيمها فرأى أن البلاد المحيطة قد تم فتحها، وأن الأراضي فيء فلا يستحق الفاتحون ملك أعيانها، بل للإمام النظر فيها بما هو أصلح لإحيائها وأدوم نفعاً لجماعة المسلمين، وإنما قسم النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ما قسمه من أرض خيبر إذ رأى المصلحة في ذلك لحاجتهم حينذاك إلى الأرض. فمكثوا يتناقشون أياماً حتى قال عمر وجدت الحجة عليهم بآخر آية الحشر إذ قالت في بيان من يستحقون من الفيء: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ جَاءُو مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ﴾ . فقال عمر: ما أرى هذه الآية إلا قد عمت الخلق كلهم حتى بگداء كداء وزان سماء»: اسم جبل بأعلى مكة). ثم قال لهم الراعي عمر: تريدون أن يأتي آخر الناس ليس لهم شيء، فما لمن بعدكم؟ ولولا آخر الناس ما فتحت قرية إلا قسمتها كما قسم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خيبر. فقرر عمر أن تبقى الأراضي والأنهار لأهلها وعمالها، وأن يفرض عليها الخراج. ثم أمر أن يفعل كذلك بأراضي مصر لما وقع فيها نظير هذا الخلاف بين الزبير بن العوام وعمرو بن العاص أمير مصر.

ومن الواضح أن هذا الاتجاه الحكيم من عمر في التمييز بين الغنائم الحربية المنقولة وبين الأراضي إنما كان تمسكاً بدلائل النصوص، وجمعاً بينها وإعمالاً لكل منها بتنزيله على منزله الذي يرشد إليه النظر الجامع السديد لا كما يوهمه كلام بعض المتوهمين اليوم من أنَّ خالف عمر في هذه القضية نصوص الشريعة ويعدون هذه المخالفة بزعمهم عبقرية اجتهادية ! فقد رأيت بما نقلناه أن عمر كانت حجته النص القرآني نفسه الذي أفحم به مخالفيه وأثبت رجحان فهمه فيه، وكان على رأيه كبار فقهاء الصحابة كعلي ومعاذ رضي الله عنهما. ومن هنا اختلفت الاجتهادات في حكم الأراضي التي يفتحها الجيش الإسلامي عنوة على ثلاثة مذاهب : مذهب يرى أنها تقسم بعد الخمس على الجيش الفاتح كالغنائم المنقولة، وإلى هذا ذهب الاجتهاد الشافعي.
Third Chapter: The Stages of Development of Islamic Jurisprudence and its Characteristics. And the difference between ghanimah and fay' in legal terminology: ghanimah is what is taken from the enemy combatant by force of arms, and fay' is what the enemies leave due to terror, or pay out of compulsion and domination, and it is not taken from them by galloping horses and the assault of the army in military battles. So fay' includes taxes imposed on them such as jizyah on persons and kharaj on lands. And it is established in the Sunnah that when the Prophet, peace be upon him, conquered Khaybar, and it was conquered by force not by truce, and its combatant inhabitants submitted to the ruling of expulsion - its lands were counted as fay', and the Prophet set aside half (or a fifth), leaving it for emergencies and calamities, and divided the remainder among the conquerors. When the Sawad of Iraq was conquered in the caliphate of Umar, the conquerors demanded the division of its lands among them like ghanimah, and Umar's opinion was that it was not permissible to divide them, so he gathered the people and consulted them. The majority opinion was to divide it, except for Ali, Uthman, Talhah, and Mu'adh ibn Jabal, who shared Umar's opinion. Mu'adh said to him: 'If you divide it, the great revenue will be in the hands of these people, then they will perish, and it will go to one man or woman, then after them will come people who will fill a great role in Islam - they will have good and beneficial service in Islam - and they will find nothing, so consider a matter that encompasses both the first and the last of them.' The conquerors insisted on demanding the division of the lands after khums, using the argument of what the Prophet did with Khaybar, but Umar refused to divide them, holding that the surrounding lands had been conquered, and the lands are fay', so the conquerors do not deserve ownership of the lands themselves; rather, the Imam has discretion over them according to what is best for their cultivation and most enduring benefit for the Muslim community. The Prophet only divided what he divided of the land of Khaybar because he saw the maslahah in that due to their need at that time for land. They continued discussing for days until Umar said: 'I found the proof against them in the last verse of Surah al-Hashr, which states regarding those who deserve fay': "And those who came after them." So Umar said: 'I do not see this verse except that it includes all people, even [someone at] Kadā' and [someone at] Samā'' (a mountain above Makkah). Then Umar said to them: 'You want the later people to come and have nothing, so what for those after you? If it were not for the later people, I would not have opened any town except that I would have divided it as the Messenger of Allah divided Khaybar.' So Umar decided that the lands and rivers should remain for their occupants and workers, and that kharaj should be imposed on them. Then he ordered the same to be done with the lands of Egypt when a similar dispute occurred between al-Zubayr ibn al-Awwam and Amr ibn al-As, the governor of Egypt. It is clear that this wise direction of Umar in distinguishing between movable war booty and lands was adherence to the textual proofs, and combining them and implementing each by placing it in its proper context to which sound comprehensive reasoning guides, not as the speech of some deluded people today insinuates that Umar contradicted the texts of Shari'ah in this matter, and they consider this contradiction, as they claim, a genius of ijtihad! Indeed, as we have transmitted, Umar's proof was the Quranic text itself with which he silenced his opponents and proved the preponderance of his understanding, and the great jurists among the Companions, such as Ali and Mu'adh, were with his opinion. Hence, ijtihads differed on the ruling of lands conquered by force by the Islamic army into three schools: a school that holds that they are divided after khums among the conquering army like movable ghanimah, and this is the Shafi'i ijtihad.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a historical-legal analysis of the distinction between ghanimah (war booty taken by force) and fay' (property acquired without direct combat, such as through treaty or fear). The author defines both terms and then presents the prophetic precedent of Khaybar, where the Prophet treated the lands as fay' and divided only part. The core of the passage is the extensive ijtihad of Caliph Umar regarding the conquered lands of Sawad al-Iraq. Umar refused the demand of the conquerors to divide the lands as ghanimah, arguing that the lands are fay' and belong to the Muslim community as a whole. He was supported by senior Companions like Ali and Mu'adh. His main evidence was verse 10 of Surah al-Hashr, which mentions those who come after the early emigrants, indicating that fay' should benefit future generations. The passage emphasizes that Umar did not contradict the texts but applied them with comprehensive reasoning. It concludes by stating that three schools emerged: one (position of Imam Shafi'i) holds that conquered lands are divided like movable booty; the other positions (Hanafi and others) side with Umar. The author defends Umar's ijtihad against modern critics who wrongly claim he opposed the texts.

Key Terms
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): ما استخلص من العدو المحارب بقوة السلاح في المعارك الحربية بإيجاف الخيل وصولة الجيش.
الفيء (al-fay'): ما تركه الأعداء عن رعب أو أدوه عن قهر دون قتال، ويشمل الجزية والخراج والأراضي المفتوحة عنوة.
الخراج (al-kharaj): ضريبة مفروضة على الأراضي المفتوحة عنوة، تبقى لأهلها ويؤدونها لبيت المال.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا غَنِمْتُمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ فَأَنَّ لِلَّهِ خُمُسَهُ﴾
B) قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ جَاءُوا مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ يَقُولُونَ رَبَّنَا اغْفِرْ لَنَا﴾

Key Takeaway
Umar's ijtihad on conquered lands established the Hanafi principle that lands taken by force are fay' not ghanimah, preserved for the benefit of all Muslims, based on the Quranic text of Surah al-Hashr.

Legal Philosophy and Theory

The Hanafi-Maliki Dispute on Conquered Lands and the Principle of Siyasa Shar'iyya
Comparison of two ijtihads with a key conceptual distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Maliki positions on conquered lands and explain how the principle of siyasa shar'iyya justifies flexibility in ruler's decisions.

Core Idea
Conquered lands: Hanafi gives ruler discretion; Maliki makes them a permanent waqf.

This passage from al-Zarqa introduces two competing ijtihads on the disposition of conquered lands (fay'). The Maliki school views them as an inalienable waqf for all Muslims, while the Hanafi school grants the ruler broad discretion to distribute or tax based on public interest. This lesson explores both positions and introduces the key concept of siyasa shar'iyya that underlies the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two schools and their positions
Read the first two paragraphs. State what each school says about conquered lands. Maliki: waqf. Hanafi: discretionary distribution or kharaj.
These are the two ijtihads mentioned.
2
Examine the evidence for each school
The Maliki school does not give specific evidence here, but the Hanafi evidence is explicit: Prophet's practice at Khaybar (distribution) and 'Umar's practice in Sawad and Egypt (kharaj).
The Hanafi relies on historical precedent.
3
Understand siyasa shar'iyya
According to the important note later in the passage, the Hanafi position is rooted in the concept that the Prophet's actions in governance are policy, not legislation. This is the basis for the ruler's discretion.
Siyasa shar'iyya means 'Sharia-consistent policy.'
4
Evaluate the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Consider a scenario: a Muslim state conquers land. Under Maliki, it becomes a permanent waqf; under Hanafi, the ruler can choose. Which allows more adaptability? Why might the Maliki view be preferred in some contexts?
The difference has implications for land tenure and public finance.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul
The Hanafi use of siyasa shar'iyya is related to istihsan and istislah. This shows the flexibility within the Hanafi school to accommodate changing circumstances.
Istihsan is a key Hanafi principle of equity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: أدوار تطور الفقه الإسلامي ومميزاته
- ومذهب يرى أنها تكون وقفاً حبيساً على جميع المسلمين، فتوضع ثمرتها في بيت المال وتصرف إلى مصالحهم وحاجاتهم العامة. وإلى هذا ذهب الاجتهاد المالكي
;
- ومذهب يرى أنَّ أمرها يعود إلى نظر الإمام وتقديره بحسب ما يرى من الحاجة والمصلحة فإن شاء عَزَل منها الخمس أو أكثر منه البيت المال، وقسم الباقي على الفاتحين، كما فعل النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام بأرض خيبر، وإن شاء ترك الأرضين لأهلها وطرح عليها ضريبة الخراج، كما فعل عمر بسواد العراق ومصر. وإلى هذا ذهب الاجتهاد الحنفي (ر: الأموال لأبي عبيد القاسم بن سلام الفقرة / ١٤٩ و ١٥٣، وبداية المجتهد لابن رشد ٣٢٤١ ورد المحتار ج ۳ باب المغنم وقسمته).

تنبيه هام:
هذا، ولا يخفى أن القرآن لم ينص على وجوب توزيع الغنائم الحربية حتى المنقولة منها بين المجاهدين الفاتحين وإنما نصت آية الأنفال على مصارف معينة لخمس الغنائم .
وتوزيع الأخماس الأربعة الباقية على الغانمين إنما جاءت به السنة وهذا النوع من السنة يعد - بحسب قواعد الشريعة - من السياسة الشرعية والتدابير المصلحية التي يفعلها النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام بصفة ولايته العامة في الحكم والإدارة لا بصفة النبوة والتشريع، فلا تفيد حقاً تشريعياً ثابتاً لا يتبدل كحكم النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام للجدة بفريضة السدس في الميراث، بل إن لكل من يخلف النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام في هذه الولاية العامة أن يلجأ إلى تدبير آخر عند الحاجة كما كان ذلك ممكناً للنبي نفسه .
فإذا تبدلت الظروف واقتضت الحاجة نظاماً آخر للجندية تقوم فيه حقوق الجيش المجاهد لا على اقتسام الغنيمة بل على أساس إعاشة ووظائف مالية مرتبة للجند، وتكون الغنائم الحربية كلها للدولة ولا حق فيها للمقاتلين كما في زماننا وأنظمتنا اليوم، فذلك سائغ شرعاً، وهو من قبيل الاستصلاح في شؤون الإدارة العامة (ر: ف ٩/٥).
غير أن نظام توزيع الغنائم كان في صدر الإسلام هو التدبير الممكن من الوجهة المالية، وهو الأصلح أيضاً لسياسة الجهاد بالنسبة إلى العرب في ذلك الزمن من الوجهة العرفية.
Chapter Three: Stages of Development of Islamic Jurisprudence and Its Characteristics
- A school of thought that sees them as an inalienable endowment for all Muslims, so their produce is placed in the public treasury and spent on their interests and general needs. The Maliki ijtihad went to this.
- And a school of thought that sees that their matter is referred to the discretion of the Imam and his estimation according to what he sees of need and interest: if he wishes, he sets aside one-fifth or more of it for the public treasury, and divides the remainder among the conquerors, as the Prophet, peace be upon him, did with the land of Khaybar; and if he wishes, he leaves the lands to their owners and imposes the kharaj tax on them, as Umar did with the Sawad of Iraq and Egypt. The Hanafi ijtihad went to this (see: Al-Amwal by Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam, paragraphs 149 and 153; Bidayat al-Mujtahid by Ibn Rushd, p. 3241; Radd al-Muhtar, vol. 3, chapter on booty and its distribution).

Important Note:
Now, it is not hidden that the Quran did not stipulate the obligation of distributing war booty, even movable property, among the conquering mujahideen; rather, the verse of al-Anfal specified certain expenditures for one-fifth of the booty.
And the distribution of the remaining four-fifths to the warriors came only through the Sunnah. This type of Sunnah is considered - according to the rules of Sharia - from the realm of sharia policy and welfare measures that the Prophet, peace be upon him, does in his capacity as his general authority in governance and administration, not in his capacity as prophethood and legislation. Thus it does not constitute a fixed legislative right that does not change, like the Prophet's ruling for the grandmother regarding the obligatory share of one-sixth in inheritance. Rather, anyone who succeeds the Prophet in this general authority may resort to another measure when needed, just as it was possible for the Prophet himself.
So if circumstances change and necessity requires a different system for the military, where the rights of the fighting army are based not on sharing the spoils but on maintenance and regular financial salaries for the soldiers, and the war spoils all go to the state with no right for the fighters, as in our time and today's systems, then that is legally permissible, and it falls under the category of istislah (public interest) in matters of general administration (see: Fiqh, 9/5).
However, the system of distributing booty in early Islam was the feasible measure from a financial perspective, and it was also the most suitable for the policy of jihad among the Arabs at that time from a customary perspective.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's general jurisprudential introduction presents two positions on the disposition of conquered lands (fay' lands). The Maliki view holds that these lands become an inalienable waqf for all Muslims, with their produce going to the public treasury. The Hanafi view, which al-Zarqa attributes to the founder's ijtihad, gives the ruler (Imam) discretion: he may distribute the lands to the conquerors (after setting aside a portion for the treasury) as the Prophet did at Khaybar, or he may leave the lands to their original owners and impose a kharaj tax, as 'Umar did in Iraq and Egypt.

Al-Zarqa then provides a crucial clarification: the Quran only specifies the allocation of the one-fifth (khums). The distribution of the remaining four-fifths to the warriors is established by the Sunnah, but this is a Sunnah of a particular type. It belongs to 'siyasa shar'iyya' (sharia policy) and welfare measures that the Prophet undertook in his capacity as head of state, not as a legislator. Therefore, it does not create an immutable legal right like the fixed inheritance shares (e.g., the grandmother's one-sixth). Successors in authority may adopt different measures when circumstances change. This justifies modern military systems where soldiers receive salaries instead of spoils, and all captured property belongs to the state. This is an application of istislah (public interest). The original system was contextually appropriate for its time.

Key Terms
السياسة الشرعية (al-siyasa al-shar'iyya): Actions of the Prophet or ruler in executive capacity, not as legislator, aimed at public welfare, and subject to change with circumstances.
الاستصلاح (al-istislah): Considering public interest in matters of general administration, even if not explicitly mentioned in nass.
الغنائم (al-ghanaim): War booty taken from the enemy by force; here includes movable and landed property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis of the Hanafi school's position that the ruler has discretion over conquered lands?
A) A verse from the Quran explicitly granting discretion.
B) The Prophet's practice at Khaybar and Caliph 'Umar's practice in Sawad.
C) The principle that all Muslims collectively own conquered lands.
D) A consensus (ijma) of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school views conquered lands as a matter of policy (siyasa) where the ruler may choose based on public interest, unlike the Maliki waqf position.

Legal Philosophy and Theory

When the Prophet Acts as Ruler: The Legal Classification of Prophetic Actions and Its Implications for Contemporary Fiqh
Clarification of the legal status of the Sunnah on booty distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Prophet's legislative and executive actions and apply this distinction to justify changes in rulings based on changing circumstances.

Core Idea
Prophetic actions as ruler are policy, not law — they can change when circumstances change.

This lesson dives into the 'Important Note' of the passage, where al-Zarqa clarifies that the distribution of booty is based on a Sunnah that is not legislative but falls under siyasa shar'iyya. This distinction is crucial for understanding why certain rulings are flexible and subject to change, as exemplified by modern military salary systems.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two capacities of the Prophet
The text distinguishes two capacities: prophethood/nubuwwa (legislation) and general authority/wilaya 'amma (governance and administration). Actions in the first capacity create immutable rulings; actions in the second are policy measures.
This is the key conceptual distinction.
2
Analyze the evidence: the Sunnah on ghanima distribution
The Quran only specifies the khums (one-fifth) portion. The distribution of the remaining four-fifths came from the Sunnah. But this Sunnah is classified as siyasa shar'iyya, not as legislative prophecy.
The Quranic verse is Surah al-Anfal 41.
3
Understand the criterion for classification
How do we know if a Prophetic action is legislative or executive? The text gives an example: the grandmother's share of one-sixth in inheritance is a legislative ruling (tashri') because it creates a fixed right. The distribution of booty is not like that because it was a practical solution suitable for the time.
Compare to the hadith of the grandmother (Sunan Abi Dawud).
4
Apply the concept: modern example
The author explicitly applies this: today's armies are salaried, and spoils go to the state. This change is permissible under istislah (public interest). The original system was the best feasible measure at that time.
This shows how the concept is used to justify contemporary practice.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul principles
Siyasa shar'iyya is related to istihsan and istislah. The Hanafi school uses these to adapt rulings to changing circumstances while staying within the framework of Sharia.
This is an important source of flexibility in Islamic law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: أدوار تطور الفقه الإسلامي ومميزاته
- ومذهب يرى أنها تكون وقفاً حبيساً على جميع المسلمين، فتوضع ثمرتها في بيت المال وتصرف إلى مصالحهم وحاجاتهم العامة. وإلى هذا ذهب الاجتهاد المالكي
;
- ومذهب يرى أنَّ أمرها يعود إلى نظر الإمام وتقديره بحسب ما يرى من الحاجة والمصلحة فإن شاء عَزَل منها الخمس أو أكثر منه البيت المال، وقسم الباقي على الفاتحين، كما فعل النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام بأرض خيبر، وإن شاء ترك الأرضين لأهلها وطرح عليها ضريبة الخراج، كما فعل عمر بسواد العراق ومصر. وإلى هذا ذهب الاجتهاد الحنفي (ر: الأموال لأبي عبيد القاسم بن سلام الفقرة / ١٤٩ و ١٥٣، وبداية المجتهد لابن رشد ٣٢٤١ ورد المحتار ج ۳ باب المغنم وقسمته).

تنبيه هام:
هذا، ولا يخفى أن القرآن لم ينص على وجوب توزيع الغنائم الحربية حتى المنقولة منها بين المجاهدين الفاتحين وإنما نصت آية الأنفال على مصارف معينة لخمس الغنائم .

Legal Philosophy and Theory

Ahl al-Hadith vs Ahl al-Ra'y: Methodological Divergence and the Zakat al-Fitr Dispute
Historical narrative on methodological schools with a fiqh dispute example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the methodological difference between Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y, and apply the Hanafi position on Zakat al-Fitr to a practical fatwa scenario.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school follows Ahl al-Ra'y, prioritizing Shariah objectives over literal textual interpretation.

The early development of Islamic fiqh saw the emergence of two methodological approaches: strict adherence to the text (Ahl al-Hadith) and reasoned interpretation (Ahl al-Ra'y). This lesson explores the historical split and its practical impact through the issue of Zakat al-Fitr. Understanding this division is key to grasping the Hanafi method of legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Contextualize the Third Phase
Identify the historical setting where the split between literalists and rationalists emerged after the era of the Companions and Successors.
The third phase followed the period where senior Companions used both text and reasoned opinion cautiously.
2
Distinguish Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y
Define each school's core approach: Ahl al-Hadith confines itself to textual limits, while Ahl al-Ra'y uses principles (usul) and objectives (maqasid) to derive rulings.
Hanafis are the primary representatives of Ahl al-Ra'y.
3
Analyze the Zakat al-Fitr Dispute
Apply the two methodologies to the same hadith to see how each derives a different ruling – one literal, one purpose-driven.
Focus on the role of maqasid in the Hanafi reasoning.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
Determine why the Hanafi position (cash payment) is considered stronger within the school, citing istihsan and custom.
The tarjih relies on the principle that the ruling's illa (cause) is poverty relief, not the specific food items.
5
Extract the Fatwa Hierarchy
Identify the operative ruling (mufta bihi) and its authority level within the Hanafi school.
The Hanafi fatwa is based on zahir al-riwayah and confirmed by later masters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (۱۲) الدور الثالث : فريضة صلاة الصبح ركعتين، وصلاة الظهر أربع ركعات فلا مجال للبحث عن عللها . فبعض الصحابة ظهر منهم الميل إلى الاتجاه الأول تحرجاً من أن يخطئوا تطبيق أوامر الرسول الله ونواهيه. وبعض آخر - ولا سيما الذين عهد إليهم بحمل المسؤوليات - ظهر منهم الميل إلى الاتجاه الثاني. ۳/۱۲ - قال العلامة الشيخ محمد الخضري بك في كتابه القيم تاريخ التشريع الإسلامي: إن كبار الصحابة كانوا في العصر الأول يستندون في فتاواهم إلى الكتاب ثم إلى السنة فإن أعجزهم ذلك أفتوا بالرأي وهو القياس بأوسع معانيه، ولم يكونوا يميلون إلى التوسع في الأخذ بالرأي. لذلك أُثِر عنهم ذم الرأي. وقد بينا فيما مضى ما الرأي المعمول به، وما الرأي المذموم؟ ولما جاء هذا الخلف من بعدهم وُجِدَ منهم من يقف في الفتوى على الحديث ولا يتعداه فيفتي في كل مسألة بما يجده من ذلك (في الحديث النبوي)، وليست هناك روابط تربط المسائل بعضها ببعض. وَوُجِد فريق آخر يرى أن الشريعة معقولة المعاني ولها أصول يرجع إليها، فكانوا لا يخالفون الأولين في العمل بالكتاب والسنة ما وجدوا إلى ذلك سبيلاً ولكنهم لاقتناعهم بمعقولية الشريعة وابتنائها على أصول محكمة مفهومة من الكتاب والسنة كانوا لا يحجمون عن الفتوى بما يرونه أقرب إلى مقاصد الشريعة فيما لم يجدوا فيه نصاً، وفوق ذلك كانوا يحبون معرفة العلل والغايات التي من أجلها شرعت الأحكام. وربما ردوا بعض أحاديث لمخالفتها أصول الشريعة، ولا سيما إذا عارضتها أحاديث نبوية أخرى. وقد كان أكثر ظهور هذا المبدأ في أهل العراق، فكان أكثر فقهاء العراق أهل رأي وكان أكثر أهل الحجاز أهل حديث (تاريخ التشريع الإسلامي، ص ۱۰۷ - ۱۰۸ ، ببعض اختصار). الباب الثالث: أدوار تطور الفقه الإسلامي ومميزاته ١٢ / ٤ - مثال : اختلاف أهل الحديث وأهل الرأي في صدقة الفطر. ورد في الحديث الصحيح الثبوت عن عدد من الصحابة ما يفيد أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أوجب على المكلفين صدقة إلى الفقراء في نهاية شهر الصيام وأول يوم الفطر مقدارها صاع من القمح أو من الشعير أو من التمر أو من الزبيب أو (١) الأقط (۱) يخرجها كل مكلف نفسه عن وعمن يتبعه ويعوله ذكوراً وإناثاً. وسميت هذه صدقة الفطر أو زكاة الفطر، وهي عبادة مالية تقدم شكراً لله تعالى على ما يسر للمؤمنين من أداء فريضة الصيام فيها معونة للفقراء بمناسبة انتهاء الصيام وحلول عيد الفطر. هذه فذهب أهل الحديث إلى أنَّ هذه الصدقة يجب تقديمها إلى الفقراء عَيْناً من أحد هذه الأقوات التي وردت في الأحاديث النبوية، ولا يصح أداؤها ولا تبرأ الذمة بتأدية قيمة أحدها بالنقود لأنَّ نص الحديث النبوي قد عيَّن هذه الأنواع. وذهب أهل الرأي، إلى أن المقصود بهذه الصدقة ليس هو الأقوات بعينها فإنَّ أنواعها ليست محلاً للتعبد ولا يتعلق بأنواعها عرض شرعي. وإنما المقصود معونة الفقراء، وحاجتهم إلى الغذاء هم وعيالهم ،محققة فورد الحديث على المعتاد الميسور للمكلفين من الأغذية الشائعة في محيطهم . فالعبرة للمالية لا للنوعية وهم أدرى بحاجتهم في ذلك اليوم. فقد تكون حاجتهم إلى الكساء أشد ولا يجدون قيمته، والنقود صالحة لقضاء كل حاجة من أي نوع كانت فلو أعطى المكلف نقوداً تعادل قيمة أحد هذه الأنواع بمقدار الواجب صح منه ذلك . بدء استقلال علم الفقه وصيرورته اختصاصاً : ٥/١٢ - في النصف الثاني من القرن الأول الهجري ظهرت بادرة (1) الصاع مكيال يعادل (٢,٧٥) ليتراً. والأقط (بفتح فكسر) لبن محمض يجمد حتى يستحجر فيطبخ ويطبخ .به. ١٨٨
Chapter (12): The Third Phase: The obligation of the dawn prayer is two rak'ahs, and the noon prayer is four rak'ahs, so there is no room for research into their causes. Some Companions showed inclination to the first approach, out of reluctance to err in applying the commands and prohibitions of the Messenger of Allah. Others, especially those entrusted with responsibilities, showed inclination to the second approach. 3/12 - The scholar Sheikh Muhammad al-Khudari Bek said in his valuable book 'History of Islamic Legislation': The senior Companions in the first era relied in their fatwas on the Book, then on the Sunnah; if that was insufficient, they gave fatwa by opinion (ra'y), which is analogical reasoning (qiyas) in its broadest sense, and they did not tend to expand the use of opinion. Therefore, criticism of opinion is attributed to them. We have already explained what is the acceptable opinion and what is the blameworthy opinion. When the later generations came after them, some of them were found to stop in fatwa at the hadith and not go beyond it, giving fatwa in every issue based on what they found in the prophetic hadith, with no links connecting issues to one another. Another group was found who saw that the Shariah has reasonable meanings and has principles to refer to. They did not oppose the first group in acting by the Book and Sunnah as long as they found a way to do so, but due to their conviction that the Shariah is reasonable and built on solid principles understood from the Book and Sunnah, they did not hesitate to give fatwa by what they deemed closer to the objectives of the Shariah in matters where they found no text. Moreover, they loved to know the causes and goals for which rulings were legislated. Perhaps they rejected some hadiths because they contradicted the principles of the Shariah, especially if they were opposed by other prophetic hadiths. This principle appeared most in the people of Iraq, so most of the jurists of Iraq were people of opinion, and most of the people of Hijaz were people of hadith (History of Islamic Legislation, pp. 107-108, with some abridgment). The Third Chapter: Periods of Development of Islamic Fiqh and Its Characteristics. 12/4 - Example: Disagreement of Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y regarding Zakat al-Fitr. There is a soundly established hadith from a number of Companions indicating that the Messenger of Allah obligated upon those legally responsible a charity to the poor at the end of the month of fasting and the first day of Eid al-Fitr, its amount being a sa' of wheat, or barley, or dates, or raisins, or (1) aqit, to be paid by every responsible person for himself and for those he follows and supports, male and female. This is called Sadaqat al-Fitr or Zakat al-Fitr. It is a financial act of worship offered as gratitude to Allah Almighty for making it easy for believers to perform the obligation of fasting, and as assistance to the poor on the occasion of the end of fasting and the arrival of Eid al-Fitr. Thus, Ahl al-Hadith held that this charity must be given to the poor in kind from one of these food items mentioned in the prophetic hadith, and it is not valid nor does the obligation discharge by paying the value of one of them in currency because the text of the prophetic hadith specified these types. Ahl al-Ra'y held that the purpose of this charity is not the food items themselves; their types are not objects of worship nor is there a legal intent attached to their types. Rather, the purpose is to assist the poor; their need for food for themselves and their families is realized, so the hadith came based on what was customary and available to the responsible persons of common foods in their environment. So the consideration is for the monetary value, not the type, and they (the poor) are more aware of their need on that day. Perhaps their need for clothing is greater and they cannot find its value, and currency is suitable for fulfilling any need of any kind. So if a responsible person gives currency equivalent to the value of one of these types in the amount obligated, it is valid from him. The beginning of the independence of the science of fiqh and its becoming a specialization: 5/12 - In the second half of the first century Hijri, the first sign appeared. (1) The sa' is a measure equal to 2.75 liters. Aqit (with a fatha then kasra) is sour milk that is solidified until it becomes hard, then cooked and cooked with it.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative describing the third phase of the development of Islamic fiqh, focusing on the emergence of two methodological schools: Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y. The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, begins by stating that basic ritual obligations like the number of rak'ahs in prayer are fixed and not subject to independent reasoning (ra'y). He then quotes Muhammad al-Khudari Bek, explaining that the senior Companions of the Prophet used both text and reasoning, but later generations split into two groups: one that adhered strictly to hadith (Ahl al-Hadith) and another that used reason and principles to derive rulings (Ahl al-Ra'y). The Ahl al-Ra'y, predominant in Iraq, believed that the Shariah has understandable meanings and objectives (maqasid), and they were willing to go beyond the literal text when necessary. The passage then provides a concrete example: the issue of Zakat al-Fitr. Ahl al-Hadith, based on the literal wording of the hadith, insisted that the charity must be given in specific food items (wheat, barley, dates, raisins, or aqit). Ahl al-Ra'y argued that the purpose of Zakat al-Fitr is to assist the poor, and the specific food items mentioned were merely customary at the time. Therefore, paying the monetary value (qima) is permissible and fulfills the obligation. This example illustrates the practical difference between the two methodologies. The passage ends with a note about the beginning of fiqh as an independent science in the second half of the first century.

Key Terms
أهل الحديث (Ahl al-Hadith): The group of scholars who rely strictly on the literal texts of hadith and do not go beyond them in deriving rulings, avoiding personal opinion.
أهل الرأي (Ahl al-Ra'y): The group of scholars who, while accepting Quran and Sunnah, use reasoned opinion (ra'y) and analogy (qiyas) to derive rulings, especially in the absence of explicit texts.
صدقة الفطر (Sadaqat al-Fitr): An obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, consisting of a specified amount of staple food (or its value) for each Muslim, to support the poor on Eid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Ra'y, why is it permissible to pay the value of Zakat al-Fitr in cash instead of giving the specific food items mentioned in the hadith?
A) Because the hadiths are not authentic.
B) Because the purpose is to assist the poor, and the specific items were customary, not obligatory types.
C) Because cash is easier for the giver.
D) Because the Prophet later abrogated the rule.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, as the heir of Ahl al-Ra'y, bases its rulings on the objectives of Shariah, allowing flexibility in matters like Zakat al-Fitr payment.

Dispute on Cash for Sadaqat al-Fitr: Literalism vs. Purpose
Example of inter-school disagreement on cash value for Fitr charity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ta'lil (purposive reasoning) to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on Sadaqat al-Fitr from the Ahl al-Hadith position, and evaluate the legal implications for modern fatwa.

Core Idea
Hanafis permit cash for Sadaqat al-Fitr because the law's purpose is aiding the poor, not the specific food types.

This passage illustrates a classic methodological conflict between Ahl al-Hadith (literalists) and Ahl al-Ra'y (Hanafis) over the permissibility of giving cash value instead of specified food items for Sadaqat al-Fitr. Understanding this dispute requires discerning when a textual detail is legally operative vs. when it is circumstantial and subordinate to the underlying purpose (maqsad). As a mufti, you must recognize how such methodological commitments shape fatwa outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Determine the exact point of disagreement: whether Sadaqat al-Fitr must be given in specific food items (in-kind) or whether cash value is permissible.
The dispute is not about the obligation itself but the mode of fulfillment.
2
Extract each school's position
State the Hanafi (Ahl al-Ra'y) position: cash value is valid. State the Ahl al-Hadith position: only in-kind food items are valid.
Ahl al-Hadith here represents the Shafi'i and Hanbali approaches.
3
Analyze the argument structure
For Ahl al-Hadith, the core proof is the literal text of the hadith specifying food. For Hanafis, the core proof is the underlying purpose (maqsad) of aiding the poor, with the food items being customary, not devotional.
Hanafis use ta'lil (reasoning based on 'illah) to prioritize purpose over literal wording.
4
Apply the Hanafi framework
Use the legal definition of Sadaqat al-Fitr: sabab (end of Ramadan), mahall (mukallaf), shart (surplus), athar (obligation). Note that the 'illah is the need of the poor, not the specific food.
This framework shows that the types are not intrinsic to the obligation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view (mufta bihi) permits cash value. In fatwa, one must follow this unless constrained by local practice or necessity.
This is a clear example of when to apply a more flexible ruling based on maqsad.

مثال : اختلاف أهل الحديث وأهل الرأي في صدقة الفطر. ورد في الحديث الصحيح الثبوت عن عدد من الصحابة ما يفيد أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أوجب على المكلفين صدقة إلى الفقراء في نهاية شهر الصيام وأول من يوم الفطر مقدارها صاع من القمح أو من الشعير أو من التمر أو من الزبيب أو (١) الأقط (۱) يخرجها كل مكلف نفسه عن وعمن يتبعه ويعوله ذكوراً وإناثاً. وسميت هذه صدقة الفطر أو زكاة الفطر، وهي عبادة مالية تقدم شكراً لله تعالى على ما يسر للمؤمنين من أداء فريضة الصيام فيها معونة للفقراء بمناسبة انتهاء الصيام وحلول عيد الفطر. هذه فذهب أهل الحديث إلى أنَّ هذه الصدقة يجب تقديمها إلى الفقراء عَيْناً من أحد هذه الأقوات التي وردت في الأحاديث النبوية، ولا يصح أداؤها ولا تبرأ الذمة بتأدية قيمة أحدها بالنقود لأنَّ نص الحديث النبوي قد عيَّن هذه الأنواع. وذهب أهل الرأي، إلى أن المقصود بهذه الصدقة ليس هو الأقوات بعينها فإنَّ أنواعها ليست محلاً للتعبد ولا يتعلق بأنواعها عرض شرعي. وإنما المقصود معونة الفقراء، وحاجتهم إلى الغذاء هم وعيالهم ،محققة فورد الحديث على المعتاد الميسور للمكلفين من الأغذية الشائعة في محيطهم . فالعبرة للمالية لا للنوعية وهم أدرى بحاجتهم في ذلك اليوم. فقد تكون حاجتهم إلى الكساء أشد ولا يجدون قيمته، والنقود صالحة لقضاء كل حاجة من أي نوع كانت فلو أعطى المكلف نقوداً تعادل قيمة أحد هذه الأنواع بمقدار الواجب صح منه ذلك .(1) الصاع مكيال يعادل (٢,٧٥) ليتراً. والأقط (بفتح فكسر) لبن محمض يجمد حتى يستحجر فيطبخ ويطبخ به.
Example: Disagreement of Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y regarding Sadaqat al-Fitr. It is reported in an authentic hadith from a number of companions that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, obligated upon the legally responsible persons charity to the poor at the end of the month of fasting and the beginning of the day of Eid al-Fitr, the amount of which is a sa' of wheat or barley or dates or raisins or (1) aqt (2). Every legally responsible person gives it on behalf of himself and those he follows and supports, males and females. This is called Sadaqat al-Fitr or Zakat al-Fitr, and it is a financial worship offered as thanks to Allah Almighty for making it easy for the believers to perform the obligatory fasting, and as assistance to the poor on the occasion of the end of fasting and the arrival of Eid al-Fitr. Then Ahl al-Hadith held that this charity must be given to the poor in kind from among these foodstuffs mentioned in the prophetic hadiths, and it is not valid to pay nor is the liability discharged by paying the value of any of them in money because the text of the prophetic hadith specified these types. And Ahl al-Ra'y held that the purpose of this charity is not the foodstuffs themselves, for their types are not a means of devotion (mahaall for ta'abbud) nor is there any legal purpose attached to their types. Rather, the purpose is the assistance of the poor, and their need for food for themselves and their families is realized. Thus the hadith came according to what was customary and available to the legally responsible persons from the common foods in their environment. So consideration is for the monetary value, not the type, and they (the poor) are more aware of their need on that day. It may be that their need for clothing is greater and they do not find its value, and money is suitable for fulfilling every need of any type. So if the legally responsible person gives money equal to the value of one of these types in the amount of the obligation, it is valid from him. (1) The sa' is a measure equivalent to (2.75) litres. Al-aqt (with fatha then kasra) is sour milk that solidifies until it becomes hard, then it is cooked and cooked with.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents an example of inter-school disagreement between Ahl al-Hadith (often representing the Hanbali and Shafi'i approaches) and Ahl al-Ra'y (representing the Hanafi approach) regarding the permissibility of giving cash in lieu of specific food items for Sadaqat al-Fitr. The Hanafi position (Ahl al-Ra'y) emphasizes the underlying purpose (maqsad) of the obligation: aiding the poor. They argue that the specific food types mentioned in the hadith were customary at the time, not intended as fixed devotional (ta'abbudi) categories. Since the poor's need may vary, money provides flexibility and fulfills the intent more effectively. Ahl al-Hadith adhere to the literal text, insisting on the exact specified items. This illustrates the broader methodological tension between textual literalism and purposive reasoning in Islamic legal theory.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (Sadaqat al-Fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, consisting of a sa' of staple food or its cash value.
أهل الحديث (Ahl al-Hadith): Scholars who rely primarily on hadith texts and are often literalists in interpretation.
أهل الرأي (Ahl al-Ra'y): Scholars who employ personal reasoning and analogical deduction, emphasizing the purposes of the law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the hadith explicitly allows cash.
B) Because the purpose is to aid the poor, and cash is more flexible to meet their needs.
C) Because the food items mentioned are no longer available.
D) Because cash is a stronger form of charity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits cash for Sadaqat al-Fitr because the law's purpose is the relief of the poor, and the specific food types are customary, not devotional.

The Later Distinction Between 'Ilm and Fiqh
Semantic shift between 'ilm and fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the later semantic distinction between 'ilm and fiqh and apply it to identify the role of textual knowledge versus interpretive faculty in Hanafi ijtihad.

Core Idea
'Ilm knows the texts; fiqh understands the rulings from them.

In the early period, 'ilm and fiqh were nearly synonymous. Over time, 'ilm became reserved for knowledge of the texts themselves (the raw material), while fiqh came to denote the faculty of deriving rulings from those texts. This shift is not merely semantic—it shapes how Hanafi scholars approach ijtihad and the hierarchy of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Locate 'ilm and fiqh in the Arabic passage and note their traditional meanings before the shift.
Historically, fiqh included all religious knowledge.
2
Identify the later meanings
The passage states that 'ilm became 'knowledge of the texts' and fiqh became 'the faculty of understanding rulings from those texts'. Paraphrase each.
The author uses riwayah vs dirayah as equivalents.
3
Compare with the sunnah/hadith parallel
The passage mentions a similar split between sunnah and hadith. Reflect on how these pairs parallel each other: one term for the source/report, the other for the normative practice or interpretive faculty.
This underscores the importance of both transmitted knowledge and reasoned understanding.
4
Apply to Hanafi ijtihad
Explain why a Hanafi mujtahid needs both 'ilm (knowing the hadith) and fiqh (the ability to derive rules).
This distinction supports the Hanafi emphasis on ra'y and qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧/١٢ - وفي هذا العصر افترق لفظ «العلم عن لفظ «الفقه» في الدلالة، فأصبح يراد من العلم معرفة النصوص ؛ ومن الفقه : ملكة فهم الأحكام من تلك النصوص وبتعبير آخر انصرف العلم إلى «الرواية»، والفقه إلى معنى «الدراية كما افترق لفظ «السنة عن لفظ «الحديث» في الدلالة على نحو ما بيناه في مطلع البحث عن السنة (ف ٣/٣).

In other words, 'ilm turned to 'riwayah' (narration), and fiqh to the meaning of 'dirayah' (understanding), just as the word 'sunnah' separated from the word 'hadith' in meaning, in the way we explained at the beginning of the discussion on the Sunnah (section 3/3).
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage notes a terminological shift in the later period of Islamic scholarship: the words 'ilm (knowledge) and fiqh (jurisprudence) originally overlapped, but later became distinct. 'Ilm came to mean knowledge of the texts (the transmitted sources, i.e., Quran and hadith), while fiqh came to mean the faculty (malakah) of deriving rulings from those texts through understanding and reasoning. This parallels another shift: the distinction between 'sunnah' and 'hadith', where sunnah became the normative practice and hadith the verbal report. For the Hanafi scholar, fiqh is the active process of deriving law, not just memorizing texts, which aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on ra'y and qiyas. This distinction is foundational for usul al-fiqh and the role of the mujtahid.

Key Terms
العلم (al-'ilm): Knowledge of the texts (nusus) themselves, equivalent to riwayah (narration).
الفقه (al-fiqh): The faculty (malakah) of understanding rulings from the texts, equivalent to dirayah (understanding).

Key Takeaway
The later distinction between 'ilm (textual knowledge) and fiqh (faculty of understanding) is essential for the methodology of ijtihad: a mujtahid must possess both.

The Modern Distinction Between 'Ilm and Fiqh: Implications for Iftaa
Clarifying the modern terminological shift between 'ilm and fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'ilm and fiqh as used in modern legal terminology and explain the implications of this distinction for a mufti's methodology.

Core Idea
Modern usage: 'ilm is textual knowledge; fiqh is juristic understanding. A mufti must master both.

This passage from Mustafa al-Zarqa clarifies a crucial terminological shift in Islamic sciences. Originally overlapping, 'ilm and fiqh later diverged: 'ilm came to denote knowledge of the texts (riwaya), while fiqh became the faculty of deriving rulings from them (diraya). Understanding this shift is essential for any student of fiqh or iftaa, as it directly impacts how a mufti approaches a legal question.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Locate the words 'ilm and fiqh in the passage. Note that they are presented as having formerly been used interchangeably but now separated in meaning.
The passage contrasts them as 'knowledge of texts' vs. 'understanding rulings'.
2
Trace the shift in connotation
Recognize the direction of the shift: 'ilm now points to riwaya (narration), while fiqh points to diraya (discernment). This is not a reversal but a specialization.
The author explicitly says 'ilm turned to riwaya and fiqh to diraya.
3
Connect to the parallel distinction
The passage mentions that the same separation occurred between sunnah and hadith. Consider why this analogy is used: sunnah is the practice, hadith is the narrated report—similar to fiqh (understanding) vs. 'ilm (texts).
This reinforces the idea that the raw material (texts) is distinct from the processed understanding (rulings).
4
Apply to the role of a mufti
A mufti must first acquire 'ilm (mastery of texts) and then develop fiqh (the ability to extract rulings). Without 'ilm, there is no foundation; without fiqh, there is no correct derivation.
Implication: Modern iftaa requires both rigorous textual study (riwaya) and deep juristic reasoning (diraya).

Source Text

In other words, 'ilm turned to 'narration' (riwaya), and fiqh to 'discernment' (diraya), just as the term sunnah separated from the term hadith in connotation as we explained at the beginning of the discussion on sunnah (section 3/3).
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage explains a critical terminological development in Islamic sciences. Originally, 'ilm (knowledge) and fiqh (jurisprudence) were used interchangeably, but later they became distinct. 'Ilm now refers to the memorization and transmission of texts (riwaya), while fiqh refers to the ability to derive and understand legal rulings from those texts (diraya). This mirrors the distinction between sunnah (the underlying practice) and hadith (the narrated report). For the Hanafi tradition, fiqh as diraya emphasizes the role of reasoning and ijtihad.

Key Terms
العلم (al-‘ilm): Knowledge, specifically textual knowledge and narration (riwaya).
الفقه (al-fiqh): Jurisprudence, the faculty of understanding and deriving rulings from texts (diraya).
الرواية (al-riwaya): Narration, transmission of texts.
الدراية (al-diraya): Discernment, deep understanding and critical analysis.

Key Takeaway
The modern terminological shift—'ilm as textual riwaya and fiqh as juristic diraya—is essential for understanding the complementary skills a mufti must develop.

The Companions' Ijtihad: Literal vs. Purposive Interpretation
Illustration of ijtihad diversity in the Prophet's era.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that both literal and purposive interpretations are valid ijtihads when the Prophet approved both.

Core Idea
Prophetic approval of both interpretations validates ijtihad based on zahir and maqasid.

This lesson examines the first example from Mustafa al-Zarqa's discussion: the Companions' differing responses to the Prophet's command during the Battle of the Trench. The Prophet's approval of both groups demonstrates that ijtihad based on literal text (zahir) and ijtihad based on underlying purpose (talil) are both valid. This is foundational for understanding the Hanafi school's broader methodology of balancing text with reason.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
The Prophet ordered the Companions not to pray Asr until at Banu Qurayza. On the way, Asr time arrived. The Companions split: some prayed on the way (purposive interpretation) and others delayed until arrival (literal interpretation).
2
Identify the two methodologies
The first group understood the command as urging haste (talil by purpose), while the second group took it literally (zahir).
This reflects the core difference between Ahl al-Ra'y and Ahl al-Hadith.
3
Analyze the Prophet's response
The Prophet did not reprimand either group; he approved both. This establishes that ijtihad based on either approach is valid.
This is a key argument for the Hanafi school's acceptance of reasonable ijtihad despite textual disagreement.
4
Connect to Hanafi usul
The Hanafi school, while generally following Ahl al-Ra'y, recognizes the validity of both. This incident supports the principle that differences in ijtihad are not necessarily errors.
This is often cited to show that ikhtilaf among mujtahids is a mercy.
