المدرستين .

٨/١٢ - المثال الأول تعليل الأمر الصريح:
روى البخاري ومسلم أنه في عام الخندق أمر الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم أصحابه بالتوجه إلى بني قريظة الذين خانوا العهد قائلاً: «لا يصلين أحد العصر إلا في بني قريظة أخرجه البخاري في المغازي، ومسلم وأحمد) وفي الطريق حان وقت صلاة العصر فاختلف الصحابة فأراد بعضهم أن يتوقفوا لأداء الصلاة خشية أن يضيق الوقت عنها، ثم يتابعون المسيرة، إذ فهموا من قول الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم لهم : لا يصلين أحد العصر إلا في بني قريظة» أن المقصود به الحث على الإسراع وعدم التأخر أو التباطؤ. ورأى آخرون أن يتابعوا المسيرة، دون توقف لأداء الصلاة، عملاً بظاهر كلام الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم. وهكذا توقف الأولون فصلوا ثم تابعوا ومضى الآخرون دون توقف، فلم يتمكنوا من تأدية صلاة العصر إلا بعد وقت صلاة العشاء. ولما علم الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم بما حصل من اختلاف آرائهم لم يقل عن أحد الفريقين أنه
أخطأ، بل أقرّ كلاً منهما على ما فعل(۱).

٩/١٢ - المثال الثاني : مسألة الشاة المصراة:
والغنم
روى أبو هريرة رضي الله عنه أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن تصرية الإبل
(۲)
وقال :
لا تُصَروا الإبل والغنم فمن ابتاعها بعد فهو بخير النظرين بعد أن يحلبها : إن شاء ،أمسك، وإن شاء رَدَّها وصاعاً من تمر» (۳). فأهل الحديث يقولون يردها المشتري، وصاعاً من تمر
أن
اللبن الذي احتلبه منها، كما جاء في هذا الحديث النبوي. وأهل الرأي يقولون : إنَّ قانون ضمان المتلفات في الشريعة الإسلامية إنما هو يرد المثل في إتلاف المثليات أو القيمة في القيميات وهذا الحديث بظاهره يجعل اللبن الذي استهلكه المشتري مقدراً بغير مثله ولا قيمته. واختلف رأيهم في النتيجة وأحسن آرائهم أنه يردها مع قيمة اللبن الذي احتلبه منها وليس مع صاع من تمر لأنَّ هذا التمر قد يكون أكثر قيمة من اللبن المحلوب أو أقل.
ويؤولون الحديث المذكور بأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قدر أن اللبن المحلوب في تلك الحال يكافؤه صاع من تمر والتمر هو المال الميسور لديهم جميعاً إذ ذاك فقضى به. ولكن الأصل الواجب شرعاً في التعادل هو القيمة، فلا يفيد

(۱) ر: ابن تيمية رفع الملام عن الأئمة الأعلام (بيروت : المكتب الإسلامي، ص (٤٧ ويعلق هذا الإمام الجليل قائلاً: ... ومع ذلك فالذين صلوا في الطريق كانوا أصوب فعلاً. وانظر أيضاً زاد المعاد لابن القيم (١٣٠/٣).
(۲) التصرية ربط ضرع الناقة أو الشاة التي كانت حلوباً عندما يريد صاحبها بيعها، حتى : يختزن لبنها ويحفل ،ضرعها، ثم يعرضها للبيع ليظن بأنها غزيرة اللبن، فبعد أن يحلبها مشتريها أول مرة لا يجتمع لها لبن جديد بالقدر المعتاد لها لبن جديد بالقدر المعتاد في الشاة الحلوب. وهو غش بالتغرير يوهم صفة كاذبة .
(۳) رواه البخاري في البيوع ۹۲/۳ ، ومسلم في البيوع ١١٥٥/٣.
Appendix to Chapter Twelve: Clarifications on the difference between Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y. We presented in Chapter (2/12) that the scientific basis for the difference between the two schools of Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y existed among the noble Companions themselves regarding the inference from legal texts. We will give two examples that clarify the difference in methodology of each of the two groups, one from the Prophetic era and the second from after the emergence of the two schools. 8/12 - First example: Reasoning of an explicit command: Bukhari and Muslim narrated that in the year of the Trench, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered his companions to go to Banu Qurayza who had broken the covenant, saying: 'Let none of you pray Asr except at Banu Qurayza.' On the way, the time of Asr prayer came, so the companions differed. Some wanted to stop to perform the prayer for fear that its time would become narrow, then continue the march, because they understood from the Messenger's statement that the intended meaning was urging haste and not delaying or slowing down. Others saw that they should continue the march without stopping for prayer, acting on the apparent meaning of the Messenger's words. Thus the first group stopped, prayed, then continued, while the others went on without stopping, and they were unable to perform Asr prayer until after the time of Isha prayer. When the Messenger learned of the difference of opinion, he did not say that either group was wrong; rather, he approved each of them for what they did (1). 9/12 - Second example: The issue of the musarrah sheep: Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated that the Messenger of Allah forbade tasriyah of camels and sheep and said: 'Do not tie the udders of camels and sheep. Whoever buys such an animal has two options after milking it: if he wishes, he may keep it, and if he wishes, he may return it along with a sa' of dates' (3). Ahl al-Hadith say that the buyer returns it along with a sa' of dates for the milk he milked, as stated in this prophetic hadith. Ahl al-Ra'y say: The principle of liability for damages in Islamic law is to return the like in fungible things and value in non-fungibles. This hadith, in its apparent meaning, makes the milk consumed by the buyer measured by something other than its like or its value. They differed in opinion on the outcome, and the best of their opinions is that he returns it with the value of the milk he milked, not with a sa' of dates, because this dates might be more valuable than the milk or less. They interpret the aforementioned hadith as the Prophet estimating that the milk in that situation was equivalent to a sa' of dates, and dates were the readily available wealth among them at that time, so he ruled by it. But the obligatory principle in Sharia for equivalence is value, so it does not avail. (1) See: Ibn Taymiyyah, Raf' al-Malam 'an al-A'immah al-A'lam, p. 47. He comments: 'Nevertheless, those who prayed on the way were more correct in action.' Also see Zad al-Ma'ad by Ibn al-Qayyim, 3/130. (2) Tasriyah is tying the udder of a milking she-camel or ewe when its owner wants to sell it, so that its milk accumulates and its udder swells, then he offers it for sale to make it appear that it has abundant milk. After the buyer milks it the first time, no new milk collects in the usual amount for a milking animal. It is deception by fraud suggesting a false quality. (3) Narrated by Bukhari in Buyu', 3/92, and Muslim in Buyu', 3/1155.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a historical and methodological clarification of the differences between Ahl al-Hadith (literalists) and Ahl al-Ra'y (rationalists). The author, Mustafa al-Zarqa, presents two examples to illustrate that this difference existed even during the Prophet's time and was accepted by him. The first example shows that some Companions interpreted a command according to its underlying purpose (talil), while others followed its literal wording (zahir). The Prophet approved both, indicating that ijtihad based on either approach is valid. In Hanafi thought, this validates the use of istihsan and maqasid, which are central to Ahl al-Ra'y methodology. The second example discusses the hadith about tasriyah: Ahl al-Hadith take the textual compensation (sa' of dates) as a binding rule, while Ahl al-Ra'y argue that general principles of liability (damages must be equivalent) override the specific textual determination, viewing the sa' as a historical approximation. This demonstrates the Hanafi preference for applying general legal maxims over literal exceptions when custom and equity demand. The passage underscores that both schools are rooted in prophetic approval and that ikhtilaf is a mercy.

Key Terms
أهل الحديث (Ahl al-Hadith): Those who adhere strictly to the apparent text of hadith without engaging in extensive rational interpretation.
أهل الرأي (Ahl al-Ra'y): Those who employ reason, analogy, and juristic preference (istihsan) in deriving rulings, beyond the literal text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the first group of Companions pray Asr on the way to Banu Qurayza?
A) They feared missing the prayer time and understood the Prophet's order as encouragement to hurry.
B) They were tired and wanted a break.
C) They rejected the Prophet's command.
D) They did not understand the command.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's approval of both literal and purposive interpretations establishes the validity of diverse ijtihad within the bounds of sincere effort.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
10 min
Text vs. Principle: The Musarrah Hadith and Hanafi Istihsan
Contrast between literal adherence and principled interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to override the literal text of a hadith when it conflicts with general legal principles.

Core Idea
Hanafis interpret 'sa' of dates' as a historical approximation, not a binding legal norm, using istihsan.

This lesson examines the second example from al-Zarqa: the hadith on tasriya (tying udders). Ahl al-Hadith take the compensation of a sa' of dates as a fixed rule. Ahl al-Ra'y argue that general principles of liability (damages must be equivalent) require returning the value of the milk, not dates. This demonstrates the Hanafi use of istihsan to prefer a general principle over a specific textual ruling when the text was based on custom that has changed.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hadith on tasriya
The Prophet forbade tying udders and gave the buyer the option to return the animal with a sa' of dates as compensation for the milk taken.
This implies the milk is compensated by a fixed measure of dates, regardless of value.
2
Identify the Ahl al-Hadith position
They follow the literal text: the buyer returns the animal and gives a sa' of dates, no matter what the milk is worth.
This is a literal application of the hadith.
3
Identify the Ahl al-Ra'y position
They invoke the general principle of damages: the milk must be compensated by its value (qimah). They view the sa' of dates as a historical approximation based on the common availability of dates at that time.
This is istihsan: preferring a general principle over a specific text that may be based on custom.
4
Analyze the Hanafi reasoning
Hanafis argue that the text (sa' of dates) is not a universal legal norm but a case-specific determination. The general principle of value equivalence in damages is stronger. Thus, the buyer must return the value of the milk, not dates.
This shows how Hanafis use istihsan to reconcile texts with fundamental legal principles.

Key Terms
تصرية (tasriya): A fraudulent practice of tying the udder of a milking animal before sale to give the impression of abundant milk; a form of deception (ghish).
أهل الحديث (Ahl al-Hadith): Those who adhere strictly to the apparent text of hadith without engaging in extensive rational interpretation.
أهل الرأي (Ahl al-Ra'y): Those who employ reason, analogy, and juristic preference (istihsan) in deriving rulings, beyond the literal text.

Legal Philosophy and Theory

Meaning of Ra'y and the Real Difference Between Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y
Clarifying the true meaning of 'ra'y' and the methodological differences between the two schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-ra'y in the Hanafi tradition and explain the actual methodological difference between Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y, distinguishing it from common misconceptions.

Core Idea
Al-ra'y is disciplined legal reasoning, not arbitrary opinion; the schools differ in methodology, not in rejecting authentic hadith.

This passage from Mustafa al-Zarqa's 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm' clarifies a fundamental misunderstanding about the Hanafi school's use of ra'y (opinion). Many assume that Ahl al-Ra'y prioritize qiyas over authentic hadith, but the author demonstrates that the real difference lies in methods of istidlal and in assessing hadith authenticity. This lesson unpacks the precise meaning of ra'y and the nature of the historical debate.

Guided Path
1
Define ra'y
Start by understanding what ra'y means in this context. The author emphasizes that it is not arbitrary opinion, but disciplined reasoning based on Sharia texts, objectives, and principles.
The term is often misunderstood by those unfamiliar with Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the components of ra'y
Based on the quote from Muhammad Abu Zahra, list the juristic tools that fall under ra'y: qiyas, istihsan, al-masalih al-mursalah, and urf.
This shows the breadth of ra'y as a methodology.
3
Examine the common misconception
Identify the false claim that Ahl al-Ra'y reject authentic hadith in favor of qiyas. The author calls this a 'ignorance of the facts'.
All four imams follow the principle: 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab.'
4
Analyze the true difference
The real difference is in the methodology of istidlal (inference) from the Sunnah and in the assessment of hadith authenticity (sihha). Scholars may disagree on the strength of a chain or the interpretation of a text.
This methodological difference is at the core, not a rejection of hadith.
5
Consider the geographical interpretation
The author discusses the common geographical explanation (Iraqi vs. Hijazi contexts) but implies it is secondary to the methodological difference.
Reflect on how environment might influence but not determine the methodology.

ملحق بالفصل (۱۲) أهل الحديث وأهل الرأي
الحديث الوارد في الموضوع أنه حكم عام، وإنما هو لحادثة بعينها. أما الحكم العام فيرجع فيه إلى الأصل.
هذان مثلان نموذجيان لاختلاف أهل مدرسة الحديث ومدرسة الرأي، وهناك أمثلة فيها غلو صارخ من أهل الحديث لا يقبله الذوق الفقهي البصير بمقاصد الشريعة، كما أنه لم يخل أهل الرأي في بعض مسائلهم من غلو في تأويل بعض الأحاديث بما يخرج عن المعتاد في فهم الخطاب، ويظهر فيه التكلف أو التمحل.
معنى «الرأي» :
١٠/١٢ ـ وهنا يجدر التنبيه إلى ناحية مهمة، وهي أن المقصود بالرأي عندما نقول: (أهل الرأي وأهل الحديث ليس هو تقرير الأحكام بالتشهي والهوى أو ما يختاره المفتي والقاضي بعقله المجرد دون تقيد بشيء من نصوص الشريعة ومقاصدها العامة التي سبق بيانها في القسم الأول من هذا البحث كما قد يتوهمه من لا علم له. وإنما المراد بالرأي لدى أهل الرأي عند سكوت النص، أو لأجل فهمه وتطبيقه) هو النظر في علة النص وغايته وسبب وروده لمعرفة المراد به من أجل حسن تطبيقه تطبيقاً صحيحاً. وفي حالة عدم النص فإنَّ المراد بالرأي الرجوع إلى مقاصد الشريعة وميزان المصالح والمفاسد بنظر الشارع (لا) بنظر الشخص وهواه كما تقدم بيانه .
يقول الأستاذ الجليل محمد أبو زهرة رحمه الله :
إنَّ المراجع لفتاوى الصحابة والتابعين .. يفهم من معنى الرأي ما يشمل اعتماد الفقيه في فتواه على ما عُرف من الدين بروحه العام، أو ما أحكامه في جملتها في نظر المفتي، أو ما يكون مشابهاً لأمر منصوص عليه فيها .. وعلى ذلك يكون الرأي شاملاً للقياس والاستحسان والمصالح المرسلة والعرف من كتاب: «مالك»، ص ١٤٩، باختصار).
يتفق مع

ومن ثم نصل إلى نتيجة مهمة
هي أن الاختلاف بين مدرستي الرأي
وأهل الحديث ليس في أن أهل الرأي يرفضون العمل بالحديث النبوي إذا صحيح الثبوت، ويرجحون عليه العمل بالقياس أو بالرأي عموماً، وأن أهل الحديث يعملون به، فهذا التصور جهل بالحقائق. فمن المعروف الثابت لدى أهل العلم والمسجل في المراجع أن كل واحد من الأئمة الأربعة قال ونقل عنه تلاميذه قوله : إذا صح الحديث فهو مذهبي. ولكن قد يختلفون في صحة أحد الأحاديث وضعفه، لأن أنظار المجتهدين قد تختلف بالنسبة إلى سند الحديث (سلسلة رواته كما قد تختلف في فهم نصه .
فالخلاف الحقيقي بين أهل الرأي وأهل الحديث إنما هو في منهجية الاستدلال بالسنة النبوية كما سبق بيانه .
ملاحظة حول التفسير الجغرافي لنشوء المدرستين:
/١١/١٢ - شاع بين من كتبوا في تاريخ الفقه الإسلامي تفسير جغرافي لتركز مدرسة أهل الرأي في العراق وبخاصة في الكوفة)، ومدرسة أهل الحديث في الحجاز وبخاصة في المدينة)، ولاختلاف المنهج بينهما . المعتاد في هذا المقام أن يقال: إن التوسع في استعمال الرأي من قلة رواية الحديث النبوي في العراق بادىء الأمر، ولتعقد الحياة المدنية فيه، وتشعب الأفكار والأعراف، وكثرة الحوادث التي لم يُعرف فيها مما ألجأ إلى استعمال الرأي.
نشأ
ومن
المعتاد أن يقال بأن أهل الحديث قد سُمّوا بذلك لكثرة رواية حديث الرسول بينهم في الحجاز وبخاصة في المدينة)، حيث كانت حاجتهم إلى استعمال الرأي في الاجتهاد قليلة، لندرة الحوادث المدنية المعقدة لديهم.
وهذا ما كنا قررناه فعلاً في الطبعات السابقة من هذا المدخل، جارينا
Appendix to Chapter (12): Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y

A hadith reported on a subject is a general ruling, but it is only for a specific incident. As for the general ruling, it refers back to the principle.

These are two typical examples of the difference between the People of Hadith school and the People of Opinion school, and there are examples of gross exaggeration by some of the People of Hadith that a perceptive juristic taste aware of the objectives of Sharia does not accept, just as the People of Opinion were not free from exaggeration in some of their issues in interpreting some hadiths in a way that deviates from the ordinary understanding of discourse, and where affectedness or contrivance appears.

The meaning of 'ra'y':
10/12 - It is worth noting here an important aspect: that what is meant by 'ra'y' when we say: (People of Opinion and People of Hadith is not the determination of rulings by whim and desire or what the mufti and judge choose by their bare intellect without being bound by anything from the texts of Sharia and its general objectives previously explained in the first section of this research, as those without knowledge might imagine. Rather, what is meant by 'ra'y' among the People of Opinion, when the text is silent, or for the purpose of understanding and applying it) is the consideration of the 'illa (effective cause) of the text, its purpose, and its reason for revelation in order to know what is intended by it for its correct application. And in the absence of a text, then what is meant by 'ra'y' is resorting to the objectives of Sharia and the scale of benefits and harms according to the view of the Lawgiver (not) according to personal view and whim, as previously explained.

The eminent professor Muhammad Abu Zahra, may Allah have mercy on him, says:

Indeed, one who reviews the fatwas of the Companions and the Successors ... understands from the meaning of 'ra'y' that it includes the jurist's reliance in his fatwa on what is known from the religion by its general spirit, or what its rulings in their entirety are in the opinion of the mufti, or what resembles a matter that is textually stated therein ... And accordingly, 'ra'y' includes qiyas (analogy), istihsan (juristic preference), al-masalih al-mursalah (unrestricted public interests), and custom (urf) from the book 'Malik', p. 149, summarized).

Agrees with

Then we reach an important conclusion:
That the difference between the two schools, the School of Opinion and the People of Hadith, is not that the People of Opinion reject acting upon a prophetic hadith if it is authentically established, and prefer acting upon qiyas or ra'y generally, and that the People of Hadith act upon it; this perception is ignorance of the facts. It is well-known and established among the people of knowledge and recorded in references that each of the four Imams said, and his students transmitted from him his saying: 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab.' But they may disagree on the authenticity or weakness of a particular hadith, because the views of the mujtahids may differ regarding the chain of transmission (isnad) of the hadith, just as they may differ in understanding its text.

So the real difference between the People of Opinion and the People of Hadith is merely in the methodology of inference (istidlal) from the Prophetic Sunnah, as previously explained.

A note regarding the geographical interpretation of the emergence of the two schools:
11/12 - It has become common among those who write about the history of Islamic jurisprudence a geographical interpretation for the concentration of the School of Opinion in Iraq (especially in Kufa) and the School of Hadith in the Hijaz (especially in Medina), and for the difference in methodology between them. It is customary in this context to say: The expansion in the use of ra'y arose from the scarcity of narration of Prophetic hadith in Iraq initially, and due to the complexity of civil life there, the diversity of ideas and customs, and the abundance of incidents for which no explicit text was known, which necessitated the use of ra'y.

And also it is customary to say that the People of Hadith were so named due to the abundance of narration of the Prophet's hadith among them in the Hijaz (especially in Medina), as their need to use ra'y in ijtihad was minimal, due to the rarity of complex civil incidents among them.

And this is what we had already stated in previous editions of this introduction, following along.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a methodological clarification from Dr. Mustafa al-Zarqa's 'Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm'. The author discusses the meaning of 'ra'y' (opinion) in Islamic jurisprudence, particularly as used by the Hanafi school (often called Ahl al-Ra'y). He begins by noting two typical examples of differences between the two schools, but then immediately cautions against misunderstanding the term 'ra'y'. He stresses that 'ra'y' does not mean arbitrary personal opinion or whim, but rather disciplined legal reasoning:

1. When a text exists, 'ra'y' involves examining the 'illa (effective cause), purpose, and occasion of revelation of the text to properly understand and apply it.
2. In the absence of a text, 'ra'y' means resorting to the higher objectives of Sharia (maqasid) and the balance of benefits and harms as determined by the Lawgiver, not by personal desire.

He then quotes Muhammad Abu Zahra, who explains that 'ra'y' encompasses qiyas, istihsan, al-masalih al-mursalah, and custom ('urf), as seen in the fatwas of the Companions and Successors.

A key conclusion is that the real difference between Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y is not that the latter reject authentic hadith; all four imams follow the principle 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab.' Rather, the difference lies in: (1) differing assessments of the authenticity (sihha) of a hadith due to scrutiny of its chain, and (2) differing methods of inference (istidlal) and interpretation of the text.

Finally, al-Zarqa discusses the common geographical explanation for the emergence of the two schools: Ahl al-Ra'y arose in Iraq due to fewer hadiths and more complex societal issues, while Ahl al-Hadith arose in Medina due to the abundance of hadiths and simpler circumstances. He notes that he previously supported this view in earlier editions.

Key Terms
الرأي (al-ra'y): Disciplined legal reasoning based on Sharia texts, objectives, and principles, not personal opinion
أهل الحديث (ahl al-hadith): Scholars who prioritize reliance on hadith texts and are cautious about using ra'y
أهل الرأي (ahl al-ra'y): Scholars who employ systematic legal reasoning (ra'y) when texts are silent or need interpretation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'ra'y' include?
A) Personal opinion
B) Qiyas, istihsan, masalih mursalah, urf
C) Only qiyas
D) A method used when texts exist

Key Takeaway
The real difference between Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y is in methodology of istidlal and assessment of hadith authenticity, not in rejecting authentic hadith.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
6 min
Refuting the Geographical Interpretation of Ahl al-Ra'y and Ahl al-Hadith
Critiquing and refuting the geographical theory of madhhab origins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the geographical theory of madhhab emergence and identify the methodological differences between Ahl al-Ra'y and Ahl al-Hadith.

Core Idea
The difference between Ahl al-Ra'y and Ahl al-Hadith is methodological, not geographical.

Many assume that geography determined the early schools: opinion-based jurisprudence flourished in Iraq due to few hadith, while traditionism thrived in the Hijaz due to abundant hadith. But Mustafa al-Zarqa challenges this with historical counterevidence. Let us examine his refutation and understand the true basis of difference between these two foundational approaches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common geographical theory
Restate the prevalent view: Ahl al-Ra'y arose in Iraq (Kufa) due to scarcity of hadith and complex social life, while Ahl al-Hadith arose in the Hijaz (Madina) due to abundant hadith and simpler conditions.
2
Examine al-Zarqa's four counter-arguments
List each of the four historical facts: (a) Iraq had many Companion scholars, (b) Imam Malik of Madina is considered Ahl al-Ra'y, (c) Ahmad ibn Hanbal from Iraq was Ahl al-Hadith, (d) al-Shafi'i's school cannot be geographically explained. Analyze how each refutes geographical determinism.
Pay attention to how counterexamples disprove causal claims.
3
Analyze the logical structure of the refutation
Al-Zarqa uses counterexamples to disprove necessary causation. If geography were decisive, we would not see Malik (Hijazi but opinion) and Ahmad (Iraqi but traditionalist). This is rational (aqli) critique.
This trains critical assessment of causal claims in legal history.
4
Synthesize the real basis of difference
Conclude that the genuine difference is methodological (manhajiyyat al-istidlal), not environmental. All imams accepted authentic hadith but differed in evaluating chains and interpreting texts.

الباب الثالث: أدوار تطور الفقه الإسلامي ومميزاته

وَمِنْ ثَمَّ نَصِلُ إِلَى نَتِيجَةٍ مُهِمَّةٍ، هِيَ أَنَّ الِاخْتِلَافَ بَيْنَ مَدْرَسَتِي الرَّأْيِ وَأَهْلِ الْحَدِيثِ لَيْسَ فِي أَنَّ أَهْلَ الرَّأْيِ يَرْفُضُونَ الْعَمَلَ بِالْحَدِيثِ النَّبَوِيِّ إِذَا صَحَّ ثُبُوتُهُ، وَيُرَجِّحُونَ عَلَيْهِ الْعَمَلَ بِالْقِيَاسِ أَوْ بِالرَّأْيِ عُمُومًا، وَأَنَّ أَهْلَ الْحَدِيثِ يَعْمَلُونَ بِهِ، فَهَذَا التَّصَوُّرُ جَهْلٌ بِالْحَقَائِقِ. فَمِنَ الْمَعْرُوفِ الثَّابِتِ لَدَى أَهْلِ الْعِلْمِ وَالْمُسَجَّلِ فِي الْمَرَاجِعِ أَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْأَئِمَّةِ الْأَرْبَعَةِ قَالَ وَنُقِلَ عَنْهُ تَلَامِيذُهُ قَوْلُهُ: «إِذَا صَحَّ الْحَدِيثُ فَهُوَ مَذْهَبِي». وَلَكِنَّهُمْ قَدْ يَخْتَلِفُونَ فِي صِحَّةِ أَحَدِ الْأَحَادِيثِ وَضَعْفِهِ؛ لِأَنَّ أَنْظَارَ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ قَدْ تَخْتَلِفُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى سَنَدِ الْحَدِيثِ (سِلْسِلَةِ رُوَاتِهِ) كَمَا قَدْ تَخْتَلِفُ فِي فَهْمِ نَصِّهِ.

فَالْخِلَافُ الْحَقِيقِيُّ بَيْنَ أَهْلِ الرَّأْيِ وَأَهْلِ الْحَدِيثِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ فِي مَنْهَجِيَّةِ الِاسْتِدْلَالِ بِالسُّنَّةِ النَّبَوِيَّةِ كَمَا سَبَقَ بَيَانُهُ.

مُلَاحَظَةٌ حَوْلَ التَّفْسِيرِ الْجُغْرَافِيِّ لِنُشُوءِ الْمَدْرَسَتَيْنِ:

١٢/١١ - شَاعَ بَيْنَ مَنْ كَتَبُوا فِي تَارِيخِ الْفِقْهِ الْإِسْلَامِيِّ تَفْسِيرٌ جُغْرَافِيٌّ لِتَرَكُّزِ مَدْرَسَةِ أَهْلِ الرَّأْيِ فِي الْعِرَاقِ (وَبِخَاصَّةٍ فِي الْكُوفَةِ)، وَمَدْرَسَةِ أَهْلِ الْحَدِيثِ فِي الْحِجَازِ (وَبِخَاصَّةٍ فِي الْمَدِينَةِ)، وَلِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَنْهَجِ بَيْنَهُمَا. الْمُعْتَادُ فِي هَذَا الْمَقَامِ أَنْ يُقَالَ: إِنَّ التَّوَسُّعَ فِي اسْتِعْمَالِ الرَّأْيِ نَشَأَ مِنْ قِلَّةِ رِوَايَةِ الْحَدِيثِ النَّبَوِيِّ فِي الْعِرَاقِ بَادِئَ الْأَمْرِ، وَلِتَعَقُّدِ الْحَيَاةِ الْمَدَنِيَّةِ فِيهِ، وَتَشَعُّبِ الْأَفْكَارِ وَالْأَعْرَافِ، وَكَثْرَةِ الْحَوَادِثِ الَّتِي لَمْ يُعْرَفْ فِيهَا نَصٌّ صَرِيحٌ، أَلْجَأَ إِلَى اسْتِعْمَالِ الرَّأْيِ.

وَكَذَلِكَ مِنَ الْمُعْتَادِ أَنْ يُقَالَ: بِأَنَّ أَهْلَ الْحَدِيثِ قَدْ سُمُّوا بِذَلِكَ لِكَثْرَةِ رِوَايَةِ حَدِيثِ الرَّسُولِ بَيْنَهُمْ فِي الْحِجَازِ (وَبِخَاصَّةٍ فِي الْمَدِينَةِ)، حَيْثُ كَانَتْ حَاجَتُهُمْ إِلَى اسْتِعْمَالِ الرَّأْيِ فِي الِاجْتِهَادِ قَلِيلَةً، لِنُدْرَةِ الْحَوَادِثِ الْمَدَنِيَّةِ الْمُعَقَّدَةِ لَدَيْهِمْ.

وَهَذَا مَا كُنَّا قَرَّرْنَاهُ فِعْلًا فِي الطَّبَعَاتِ السَّابِقَةِ مِنْ هَذَا الْمَدْخَلِ، جَارِيًا فِيهِ مَعَ بَعْضِ مَنْ سَبَقَنَا. لَكِنْ يَبْدُو لِلْمُتَأَمِّلِ أَنَّ هَذَا التَّفْسِيرَ لِنُشُوءِ الْمَدْرَسَتَيْنِ وَتَوَطُّنِهِمَا الْجُغْرَافِيِّ بَادِئَ الْأَمْرِ لَا يَتَّفِقُ مَعَ عِدَّةِ حَقَائِقَ تَارِيخِيَّةٍ وَفِقْهِيَّةٍ مَشْهُورَةٍ، مِنْهَا:

أ - كَانَ الْعِرَاقُ مِنْ أَسْعَدِ الْأَمْصَارِ حَظًّا بِالصَّحَابَةِ. وَكَانَتِ الْكُوفَةُ وَالْبَصْرَةُ قَاعِدَةً لِلْجُيُوشِ الْإِسْلَامِيَّةِ، وَنَزَلَ بِهَا أَكْثَرُ عُلَمَاءِ الصَّحَابَةِ (١). وَكَانَتِ الْكُوفَةُ مُقَرَّ الْخِلَافَةِ زَمَنَ عَلِيٍّ - كَرَّمَ اللَّهُ وَجْهَهُ - وَكَانَ فِيهَا قَبْلَهُ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ وَسَعْدُ بْنُ أَبِي وَقَّاصٍ وَعَمَّارُ بْنُ يَاسِرٍ، وَأَبُو مُوسَى الْأَشْعَرِيُّ وَالْمُغِيرَةُ بْنُ شُعْبَةَ وَأَنَسُ بْنُ مَالِكٍ، وَحُذَيْفَةُ بْنُ الْيَمَانِ، وَعِمْرَانُ بْنُ حُصَيْنٍ، وَكَثِيرٌ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ الَّذِينَ كَانُوا مِنْ حِزْبِ عَلِيٍّ وَمَنْ مَعَهُ كَابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ. وَهَؤُلَاءِ هُمْ حَمَلَةُ الْحَدِيثِ وَرُوَاتُهُ (٢).

هَذِهِ الْحَقِيقَةُ تَتَنَافَى مَعَ ظَنِّ قِلَّةِ الْحَدِيثِ فِي الْعِرَاقِ.

ب - إِنَّ أَشْهَرَ مُجْتَهِدٍ فِي الْحِجَازِ هُوَ مَالِكٌ بِلَا رَيْبٍ، وَفِقْهُهُ يُعَدُّ فِي مَدْرَسَةِ أَهْلِ الرَّأْيِ، عَلَى الرَّغْمِ مِنْ كَثْرَةِ رِوَايَتِهِ لِلْحَدِيثِ.

ج - إِذَا كَانَتِ الْبِيئَةُ الِاجْتِمَاعِيَّةُ فِي الْعِرَاقِ هِيَ الدَّاعِيَةَ إِلَى اللُّجُوءِ لِلرَّأْيِ، فَكَيْفَ أَنْجَبَتْ هَذِهِ الْبِيئَةُ نَفْسُهَا إِمَامَ مَدْرَسَةِ أَهْلِ الْحَدِيثِ أَحْمَدَ بْنَ حَنْبَلٍ؟

د - وَإِذَا نَظَرْنَا فِي فِقْهِ الْإِمَامِ الشَّافِعِيِّ نَرَاهُ أَقْرَبَ إِلَى أَهْلِ الْحَدِيثِ، وَلَا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُنْسَبَ هَذَا لِبِيئَتِهِ، إِذْ قَدْ عَاشَ فِي الْحِجَازِ وَالْيَمَنِ وَالْعِرَاقِ ثُمَّ مِصْرَ، وَدَرَسَ أَقْوَالَ أَهْلِ الْحَدِيثِ وَأَهْلِ الرَّأْيِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَبْرُزَ بِمَذْهَبٍ مُتَمَيِّزٍ.

١٢/١٢ - نَتِيجَةُ: إِنَّ التَّفْسِيرَ الْجُغْرَافِيَّ لِنِشْأَةِ مَدْرَسَتِي الرَّأْيِ وَالْحَدِيثِ وَتَرَكُّزِهِمَا لَا يَسْتَنِدُ إِلَى أَسَاسٍ صَحِيحٍ، بَلْ يَجِبُ أَنْ يُعْزَى الِاخْتِلَافُ فِي الْمَنْهَجِ إِلَى أَسْبَابٍ عِلْمِيَّةٍ مَحْضَةٍ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِطَرِيقَةِ الِاسْتِدْلَالِ وَمَدَى اعْتِمَادِ الْحَدِيثِ وَالْقِيَاسِ.
Chapter Three: Stages of Evolution of Islamic Jurisprudence and Its Characteristics

Hence we reach an important conclusion: that the difference between the school of opinion and the people of hadith is not that the people of opinion reject acting upon the Prophetic hadith when it is authentically established, and prefer acting upon analogy or opinion in general, while the people of hadith act upon it; this perception is ignorance of the facts. For it is well-known and established among scholars and recorded in references that each of the four imams said, and his students transmitted from him: 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my school.' But they may differ regarding the authenticity or weakness of a particular hadith, because the views of mujtahids may differ with respect to the chain of transmission of the hadith (the series of its narrators) as they may differ in understanding its text.

So the real difference between the people of opinion and the people of hadith is only in the methodology of inference from the Prophetic Sunnah, as previously explained.

A note on the geographical interpretation of the emergence of the two schools:

12/11 - A geographical interpretation has become prevalent among those who have written on the history of Islamic jurisprudence, concerning the concentration of the school of opinion in Iraq (especially in Kufa) and the school of hadith in the Hijaz (especially in Madina), and the difference in methodology between them. It is customary in this context to say that the expansion in the use of opinion arose from the scarcity of narration of Prophetic hadith in Iraq in the beginning, and due to the complexity of civil life there, the multiplicity of ideas and customs, and the abundance of incidents for which there was no explicit text, which necessitated the use of opinion.

Similarly, it is customary to say that the people of hadith were so named because of the abundance of narration of the Prophet's hadith among them in the Hijaz (especially in Madina), where their need to use opinion in ijtihad was minimal, due to the rarity of complex civil incidents among them.

And this is what we had indeed stated in previous editions of this introduction, following some of those before us. But it appears to the contemplator that this interpretation of the emergence of the two schools and their geographical settlement in the beginning does not agree with several well-known historical and jurisprudential facts, including:

(a) Iraq was one of the most fortunate regions in terms of the number of Companions. Kufa and Basra were bases for the Islamic armies, and most of the Companion scholars settled there (1). Kufa was the seat of the caliphate during the time of Ali (may God honor his face), and before him there were Ibn Mas'ud, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Ammar ibn Yasir, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba, Anas ibn Malik, Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman, 'Imran ibn Husayn, and many of the Companions who were from the party of Ali and those with him, such as Ibn 'Abbas. These are the bearers of hadith and its narrators (2).

This fact contradicts the assumption of scarcity of hadith in Iraq.

(b) The most famous mujtahid in the Hijaz is undoubtedly Malik, and his jurisprudence is considered part of the school of opinion, despite his abundant narration of hadith.

(c) If the social environment in Iraq was the cause for resorting to opinion, how did this same environment produce the imam of the school of hadith, Ahmad ibn Hanbal?

(d) If we look at the jurisprudence of Imam al-Shafi'i, we see it is closer to the people of hadith, and this cannot be attributed to his environment, for he lived in the Hijaz, Yemen, Iraq, then Egypt, and studied the statements of both the people of hadith and the people of opinion before emerging with a distinct school.

12/12 - Conclusion: The geographical interpretation of the emergence and concentration of the two schools of opinion and hadith is not based on a sound foundation; rather, the difference in methodology must be attributed to purely scientific reasons related to the method of inference and the extent of reliance on hadith and analogy.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the common geographical explanation for the emergence of the Ahl al-Ra'y (School of Opinion) and Ahl al-Hadith (School of Hadith). The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, first clarifies a common misconception: the difference between the two schools is not that one rejects authentic hadith while the other accepts it—all four imams upheld the principle that an authentic hadith overrides their own opinion. The real difference lies in the methodology of deriving rulings from the Sunnah, such as how they evaluate chains of transmission and interpret texts.

Al-Zarqa then presents the standard geographical theory: Ahl al-Ra'y arose in Iraq (especially Kufa) due to a scarcity of hadith and complex social conditions, while Ahl al-Hadith thrived in the Hijaz (especially Madina) due to abundant hadith and simpler circumstances. He acknowledges that he himself repeated this theory in earlier editions.

However, he now refutes it with four historical and jurisprudential facts: (a) Iraq actually had many Companion scholars and was a center of hadith transmission; (b) Imam Malik of Madina, despite his abundant hadith knowledge, is often associated with the school of opinion; (c) Ahmad ibn Hanbal, the leading figure of Ahl al-Hadith, came from the Iraqi environment; (d) Imam al-Shafi'i's jurisprudence is closer to Ahl al-Hadith despite his diverse geographical exposure.

Al-Zarqa concludes that the difference between the two schools should be attributed to purely methodological factors, not geography.

Key Terms
أهل الرأي (Ahl al-Ra'y): The school of early jurists who relied more on reasoned opinion and analogy (qiyas) in deriving legal rulings, especially prominent in Iraq (Kufa).
أهل الحديث (Ahl al-Hadith): The school that prioritized textual evidence (hadith) over reasoned opinion, emphasizing careful hadith criticism and limiting the use of analogy.
منهجية الاستدلال (Manhajiyyat al-Istidlal): The methodological approach to deriving legal proofs from the primary sources, particularly the Sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Zarqa, what is the real difference between Ahl al-Ra'y and Ahl al-Hadith?
A) The geographical origin.
B) The methodology of inference from the Sunnah.
C) One rejects hadith, the other accepts.
D) One uses only analogy, the other only hadith.

Key Takeaway
The difference between Ahl al-Ra'y and Ahl al-Hadith is methodological, not geographical; all four imams accepted authentic hadith.

Legal Philosophy and Theory
intermediate
8 min
Geographical Interpretation of Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y
Critique of the geographical explanation for the emergence of Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the geographical interpretation of the emergence of Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y by identifying historical counterexamples and explaining the alternative methodological explanation.

Core Idea
The difference between Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y is methodological, not geographical.

Many students assume that the division between Ahl al-Hadith (traditionists) and Ahl al-Ra'y (rationalists) arose due to regional differences—Hadith in Hijaz, Ra'y in Iraq. In this passage, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa dismantles this oversimplification with four historical facts. By critically examining these counterexamples, you will understand that the true divergence lies in two fundamental approaches to legal texts: literal adherence versus purpose-driven interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target theory
State the geographical interpretation that the author is critiquing: Ahl al-Hadith originated in the Hijaz (due to abundance of hadith) and Ahl al-Ra'y in Iraq (due to scarcity of hadith and a more complex society).
This theory is commonly found in introductory works.
2
Review the four counterexamples
List the author's four points: A) Iraq had many Companion hadith carriers; B) Imam Malik (Hijazi) is considered Ahl al-Ra'y; C) Ahmad ibn Hanbal (Iraqi) is the imam of Ahl al-Hadith; D) Imam al-Shafi'i's methodology evolved across regions.
Each point directly challenges a key assumption of the geographical theory.
3
Analyze how each counterexample refutes the theory
Explain why each point undermines the geographical explanation. For example, point A contradicts the claim of hadith scarcity in Iraq; point B shows that even in the Hijaz, a scholar could be rationalist; point C shows that environment does not determine methodology.
Focus on the logical force of each counterexample.
4
Synthesize the author's conclusion
The author concludes that the real difference is methodological: an approach that adheres strictly to the apparent text (zahir) versus an approach that gives weight to general objectives (maqasid) and wisdom.
This is not a new theory but a refinement acknowledging both approaches co-exist across regions.
5
Apply the insight to mufti practice
Recognize that a mufti must be aware of both methodological tendencies when deriving rulings, and that no madhhab is purely one or the other. The Hanafi school, while associated with ra'y, also relies on hadith, and vice versa.
This prevents simplistic characterizations when analyzing legal positions.

ملحق بالفصل (۱۲) أهل الحديث وأهل الرأي
فيه بعض من سبقنا . لكن يبدو للمتأمل أنَّ هذا التفسير لنشوء المدرستين وتوطنهما الجغرافي بادىء الأمر لا يتفق مع عدة حقائق تاريخية وفقهية
مشهورة، منها:
أ - كان العراق من أسعد الأمصار حظاً بالصحابة. وكانت الكوفة والبصرة قاعدة للجيوش الإسلامية .. ونزل بها أكثر علماء الصحابة (1) . وكانت الكوفة مقرَّ الخلافة زمن علي - كرم الله وجهه - وكان فيها قبله ابن مسعود وسعد بن أبي وقاص وعمار بن ياسر، وأبو موسى الأشعري والمغيرة بن شعبة وأنس بن مالك، وحذيفة بن اليمان، وعمران بن حصين، وكثير من الصحابة الذين كانوا من حزب علي ومن معه كابن عباس. وهؤلاء هم حملة الحديث ورواته . . » (۲)) .
هذه الحقيقة تتنافى مع ظن قلة الحديث في العراق.
ب - إِنَّ أشهر مجتهد في الحجاز هو مالك بلا ريب، وفقهه يعد في مدرسة أهل الرأي، على الرغم من كثرة روايته للحديث .
ج - إذا كانت البيئة الاجتماعية في العراق هي الداعية إلى اللجوء للرأي فكيف أنجبت هذه البيئة نفسها إمام مدرسة أهل الحديث أحمد بن
حنبل؟
د - وإذا نظرنا في فقه الإمام الشافعي نراه أقرب إلى أهل الحديث ولا يمكن أن ينسب هذا لبيئته، إذ قد عاش في الحجاز واليمن والعراق ثم مصر، ودرس أقوال أهل الحديث وأهل الرأي قبل أن يبرز بمذهب متميز.
١٢/١٢ - نتيجة :
إنَّ التفسير الجغرافي لنشأة مدرستي الرأي والحديث وتركزهما لا ينطبق على مذهب من المذاهب الأربعة. وأقرب ما ينطبق عليه هو مذهب الحنفية. لكن حتى هذا يقدح في انطباقها عليه ما قدمناه في البند (أ) آنفاً .
ويبدو لنا أن التفسير الأقرب للواقع والأبعد عن التكلف هو :
أنَّ اختلاف منهج مدرستي أهل الحديث وأهل الرأي هو مظهر لمنهجين أساسيين في التعامل مع النصوص التشريعية عموماً، قلما تخلو منهما بيئة إنسانية متحضّرة : منهج شديد التمسك بظاهر النص، ومنهج يعطي وزناً أكبر للمقاصد العامة التي بني عليها النص والحكمة المتوخاة منه.
Appendix to Chapter (12): Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y. Some of our predecessors have discussed this. But to the thoughtful observer, this interpretation of the emergence of the two schools and their initial geographical localization does not agree with several well-known historical and jurisprudential facts, including: A- Iraq was among the most fortunate regions in terms of Companions. Kufa and Basra were bases for the Islamic armies... and most of the scholarly Companions settled there (1). Kufa was the seat of the caliphate during the time of Ali - may Allah honor his face - and before him there were Ibn Mas'ud, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, 'Ammar ibn Yasir, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba, Anas ibn Malik, Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman, 'Imran ibn Husayn, and many of the Companions who were from the party of Ali and those with him, such as Ibn 'Abbas. These are the carriers and narrators of hadith (2). This fact contradicts the assumption that hadith was scarce in Iraq. B- The most famous mujtahid in the Hijaz is undoubtedly Malik, and his jurisprudence is considered within the school of Ahl al-Ra'y, despite his extensive narration of hadith. C- If the social environment in Iraq was the cause for resorting to opinion, then how did this same environment produce the imam of the Ahl al-Hadith school, Ahmad ibn Hanbal? D- If we examine the jurisprudence of Imam al-Shafi'i, we see it is closer to Ahl al-Hadith, and this cannot be attributed to his environment, as he lived in the Hijaz, Yemen, Iraq, and then Egypt, and studied the positions of Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y before emerging with a distinct madhhab. 12/12 - Conclusion: The geographical interpretation of the emergence and concentration of the schools of Ra'y and Hadith does not apply to any of the four madhhabs. The closest it applies to is the Hanafi madhhab. But even this is undermined by what we presented in point (A) above. It appears to us that the interpretation closest to reality and farthest from artifice is: that the difference in methodology between the two schools of Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y is a manifestation of two fundamental approaches in dealing with legislative texts in general, which hardly any civilized human environment lacks: an approach that adheres strictly to the apparent meaning of the text, and an approach that gives greater weight to the general objectives upon which the text was based and the wisdom intended from it.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the commonly held geographical explanation for the emergence of the two main jurisprudential schools: Ahl al-Hadith (traditionists) and Ahl al-Ra'y (rationalists). The author, Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, argues that the theory that Ahl al-Hadith originated in the Hijaz and Ahl al-Ra'y in Iraq is historically flawed. He presents four counterarguments: First, Iraq was rich in Companions who were carriers of hadith, contradicting the notion that hadith was scarce there. Second, Imam Malik, the prominent scholar of the Hijaz, is considered part of the Ahl al-Ra'y school despite his vast hadith knowledge. Third, Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, the epitome of Ahl al-Hadith, was from Iraq, the supposed cradle of rationalism. Fourth, Imam al-Shafi'i, who studied in various regions, developed a middle path. The author concludes that the real difference is methodological: one approach adheres strictly to the literal text, while the other emphasizes the broader objectives (maqasid) and wisdom behind the text. This analysis is foundational for understanding the diversity within Islamic legal thought.

Key Terms
أهل الحديث (Ahl al-Hadith): The school that adheres strictly to the apparent meaning of textual evidences (Quran and Hadith) and relies less on personal opinion or analogy.
أهل الرأي (Ahl al-Ra'y): The school that gives greater weight to the general objectives (maqasid) and wisdom of the texts, allowing for more use of personal reasoning and analogy.
التفسير الجغرافي (al-tafsir al-jughrafi): The interpretation that attributes the origin and geographic concentration of the two schools to regional factors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the main flaw in the geographical interpretation of the two schools?
A) It does not account for the role of the Umayyad caliphs.
B) It fails to recognize that both schools existed in all regions, and the real difference is methodological.
C) It ignores the influence of Persian philosophy.
D) It overemphasizes the role of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
The division between Ahl al-Hadith and Ahl al-Ra'y is fundamentally methodological, not geographical.
